### Post by skoh-fley on 2008-07-26
Hello, I've been trying to get my tablet PC to work with Ubuntu (Hardy) for more than a week now, and I'm getting very frustrated getting the touch screen / stylus to work at all.

I've searched all over the place and seen several success stories all with different methods, but none seem to work for me (a lot are old and pre-Hardy). I'm still a little new to Linux so I'm just getting the hang of everything, but I'm pretty positive I've been doing what the tutorials say.

My current xorg.conf file is:

```
# nvidia-xconfig: X configuration file generated by nvidia-xconfig
# nvidia-xconfig:  version 1.0  (buildmeister@builder3)  Thu Feb 14 18:20:37 PST 2008

Section "ServerLayout"
    Identifier     "Layout0"
    Screen      0  "Screen0"
    InputDevice    "Keyboard0" "CoreKeyboard"
    InputDevice    "Mouse0" "CorePointer"
EndSection

Section "Files"
    RgbPath         "/usr/lib/X11/rgb"
EndSection

Section "Module"
    Load           "dbe"
    Load           "extmod"
    Load           "type1"
    Load           "freetype"
    Load           "glx"
EndSection

Section "InputDevice"
    # generated from default
    Identifier     "Mouse0"
    Driver         "mouse"
    Option         "Protocol" "auto"
    Option         "Device" "/dev/psaux"
    Option         "Emulate3Buttons" "no"
    Option         "ZAxisMapping" "4 5"
EndSection

Section "InputDevice"
    # generated from default
    Identifier     "Keyboard0"
    Driver         "kbd"
EndSection

Section "Monitor"
    Identifier     "Monitor0"
    VendorName     "Unknown"
    ModelName      "Unknown"
    HorizSync       30.0 - 110.0
    VertRefresh     50.0 - 150.0
    Option         "DPMS"
EndSection

Section "Device"
    Identifier     "Device0"
    Driver         "nvidia"
    VendorName     "NVIDIA Corporation"
EndSection

Section "Screen"
    Identifier     "Screen0"
    Device         "Device0"
    Monitor        "Monitor0"
    DefaultDepth    24
    SubSection     "Display"
        Depth       24
    EndSubSection
EndSection
```

And of course I've tried adding in the various versions of the cursor, stylus and eraser sections, like

```
Section “InputDevice”
    Driver “wacom”
    Identifier “stylus”
    Option “Device” “/dev/ttyS0&#8243; #SERIAL ONLY

    Option “Device” “/dev/input/wacom” #USB ONLY
    Option “Type” “stylus”
    Option “USB” “on” #USB ONLY

    Option “ForceDevice” “ISDV4&#8243; #Tablet PC ONLY
    EndSection

    Section “InputDevice”
    Driver “wacom”
    Identifier “eraser”

    Option “Device” “/dev/ttyS0&#8243; #SERIAL ONLY
    Option “Device” “/dev/input/wacom” #USB ONLY
    Option “Type” “eraser”

    Option “USB” “on” #USB ONLY
    Option “ForceDevice” “ISDV4&#8243; #Tablet PC ONLY
    EndSection

    Section “InputDevice”

    Driver “wacom”
    Identifier “cursor”
    Option “Device” “/dev/ttyS0&#8243; #SERIAL ONLY
    Option “Device” “/dev/input/wacom” #USB ONLY

    Option “Type” “cursor”
    Option “Mode” “relative”
    Option “USB” “on” #USB ONLY

    Option “ForceDevice” “ISDV4&#8243; #Tablet PC ONLY
    EndSection
```

My machine is an HP Pavillion tx2110us (fairly new), and I read somewhere that the newer tablet PCs route their touch screens through USB now instead of serial (I've tried both methods). I'm still not sure if that means I'm supposed to leave the "Tablet PC ONLY" sections there or not, in addition to the USB ones.

Any help is really appreciated, I'm frustrated that I can't get this to work and I'm afraid it's something stupid I'm missing.

Thanks!

### Post by gali98 on 2008-07-26
Hey welcome to the forums!

You are in luck. The linux wacom was updated just recently to support our tablets (I have the tx2000z which is the online version of your tablet)
I have everything working and am planing on writing a tutorial soon.. (hopefully tomorrow)
If you can't wait till then, go to
[http://linuxwacom.sourceforge.net/](http://linuxwacom.sourceforge.net/)

and download the dev package and get going!
You are right about it being usb...
I am attaching my xorg.conf (had to rename it so I could upload it) as that will help a bit in the end, configuring, though you may have to change it a bit.
It's really not hard any more. No more patches or anything.
I will post a link to the tutorial when a make it here.
Kory

### Post by gali98 on 2008-07-27
***** UPDATED November 3, 2008 *****

NOTES:

If you are on Intrepid, the packages are already packaged in .deb format!
The release is 0.8.1-4 for the packages.
I have heard both reports of these packages working, and them not working... If you want to compile the newest version, then just move on...
From all apearences, these packages DO NOT work. As far as I can tell, this is because of HAL and fdi files.
Edit: I have found out a bit more about the whole thing... For us, hotplugging our tablets is useless (unless you normally open your lappy and disconnect you digitalizer and reconnect it.) So using the xorg.conf is the best way (it also means we can use the touchscreen and eraser)


If anyone has any idea what all that stuff is, please inform me : )
Other wise do 
```
sudo apt-get install wacom-tools xserver-xorg-input-wacom
```

***If you are getting errors when running wacomcpl that says libwacomcfg.so.0 cannot be found, then you need to run configure like so
```
./configure --enable-wacom --prefix=/usr
```

Calibration is now fixed! Now just use wacomcpl (see below!)
If you have updated and the wacom stuff stops working, you will need to recompile. All you have to do is recompile, and copy over the driver. Your Xorg.conf will stay the same unless you mess with it :)

With 0.8.1-5 there seems to be a lot of little issues fixed!
Like when using touch, sometimes after clicking (with touch) the cursor will jump up and click on the toolbar, or do weird stuff like that.
As far as I can tell it now is fixed.
If you have any issues please report them here. Thanks and enjoy!

For an update changelog, just check the linux-wacom folder you download. It is in the file Changelog.

Okay Here we go....

I want to first say that even though this looks like a lot of work, it is not really... I just explain everything very thouroughly (I can't spell) If you are a linux person then just download the source from the linux wacom site, compile it and copy the driver to the correct module section (check below) then configure xorg.conf like I show below....
If you are not don't be afraid to plunge in and get the tablet working! 

~~FINDING HELP~~
Note first I just want to say that when looking for help on this tablet series the best search to do on these forums is

"tx2*" (without the quotes) this will find you a lot more posts!

~~~~TUTORIAL FOR USB WACOM TABLET PC~~~~


I now put the Code boxes around the all terminal input so you don't have to worry about copying the > :)

```
cd ./Desktop

wget http://prdownloads.sourceforge.net/linuxwacom/linuxwacom-0.8.1-6.tar.bz2
```

(all of the apt-get commands install the packages we need and updates the system to the latest packages)

```
sudo apt-get update

sudo apt-get install build-essential libx11-dev libxi-dev x11proto-input-dev xserver-xorg-dev tk8.4-dev tcl8.4-dev libncurses5-dev

sudo apt-get upgrade

sudo apt-get install wacom-tools xserver-xorg-input-wacom

sudo apt-get purge wacom-tools xserver-xorg-input-wacom
```

Okay now you need to add the kernel headers for your kernel. Most people will just do

```
sudo apt-get install linux-headers-generic
```

to check your kernel version do:

```
uname -r
```

Some people might have the rt kernel...

```
sudo apt-get install linux-headers-rt
```

If during any time you got a notice to restart or if you have a little restart icon in the top right system try (looks kinda like a blue recycle icon) then by goodness restart. If you are not sure, then go ahead and restart just to be safe. The reason is if you update to a newer kernel, then the module won't work on restart as the module is compiled for a specific kernel.

Okay now we get to the good stuff....

```
tar xjvf linuxwacom-0.8.1-6.tar.bz2

cd linuxwacom-0.8.1-6

./configure --enable-wacom --prefix=/usr

make

sudo make install

```

If this returns an error saying "wacom" is not loaded, Do not worry. Just means you've never installed wacom before. Continue...

```
sudo cp ./src/2.6.24/wacom.ko /lib/modules/`uname -r`/kernel/drivers/input/tablet/wacom.ko
```

If you are on Intrepid,
use the following command instead:
```
sudo cp ./src/2.6.27/wacom.ko /lib/modules/`uname -r`/kernel/drivers/input/tablet/wacom.ko
```

You will now need to restart. This is necessary on Intrepid!

Okay that installed it, but now we need to configure our xserver....

Okay I will try to make this as simple as possible. Unfortunately for some reason the stylus and touch events do not go by the same event number every time so we have to go another way...
first of all If you have made any changes to
/etc/X11/xorg.conf concerning wacom delete all those changes Unless you have followed this tutorial before and know what you are doing. (make sure to also remove wacom references in the server layout section!)

Also do:
```
gedit ~/.xinitrc
```

and delete any line with "xsetwacom" at the beginning Unless you know why it is there. This will make it easier to calibrate. Save that then restart.

If when you do the command the file is blank, do not worry. Just close out of gedit and continue on.

After you restart the stylus and touch should work. If it does not, restart again. It took me like three times before it kicked in. Don't ask me why...
It should move it, though probably very  uncalibrated. Make sure you cover the entire screen to see if it moves.
If it does not move then post the results of

```
./configure --enable-wacom --prefix=/usr

make

sudo make install

sudo rmmod wacom

sudo modprobe wacom
```

and also post the contents of xorg.conf (/etc/X11/xorg.conf)

If you have got this far good!

Open up a terminal

```
gksudo gedit /etc/X11/xorg.conf &
```

(leave the terminal open...)

In the text editor add the following lines under the Synaptic InputDevice Section (check the bottom of this post for my xorg.conf to see what I mean....)



```

Section "InputDevice"
Identifier "stylus"
Driver "wacom"
Option "Type" "stylus"
Option "USB" "on"
Option "Device" "/dev/input/by-path/pci-0000:00:0b.1-usb-0:2.3:1.0-event-mouse"
Option "Button2" "3" # make side-switch a right button
Option "TopX" "225"
Option "TopY" "225"
Option "BottomX" "26300"
Option "BottomY" "16375"
EndSection

Section "InputDevice"
Identifier "touch"
Driver "wacom"
Option "Type" "touch"
Option "USB" "on"
Option "Device" "/dev/input/by-path/pci-0000:00:0b.1-usb-0:2.3:1.1-event-"
Option "TopX" "200"
Option "TopY" "225"
Option "BottomX" "4000"
Option "BottomY" "3875"
EndSection

Section "InputDevice"
Identifier "eraser"
Driver "wacom"
Option "Type" "eraser"
Option "Device" "/dev/input/by-path/pci-0000:00:0b.1-usb-0:2.3:1.0-event-mouse"
Option "USB" "on"
EndSection

```


Now Find the part that says 'Section "ServerLayout"'

In there add:

```

Inputdevice "stylus"	"SendCoreEvents"
Inputdevice "touch"	"SendCoreEvents"
Inputdevice "eraser"	"SendCoreEvents"

```

Now we need to fix the synaptic touch pad part. Since it has the word "touch" in it it is wrongly detected.
find the part that says:

```
	Identifier	"Synaptics Touchpad"
```
and change it to 

```
	Identifier	"Synaptics Pad"
```

then in the server layout section also change it****

if this is all confusing, you can download my xorg.conf to look at. It is at the bottom of this post. Do not use any other xorg.conf of mine uploaded on any other thread or post as it is probably old. 
note: if you are on another tablet (not a tx2000 series) it would not be wise to just paste my xorg into yours. It will probably not work. In fact it will probably break stuff :)
If you have the tx2000 if you just renamed it to xorg.conf and pasted it over yours, it would probably work, but I don't suggest doing it. 

Now Maximize the termial....
now in the termial type :

```
reset

dmesg | grep Wacom
```

there should be two lines similar to this:

```
[ 45.460644] input: Wacom ISDv4 93 as /devices/pci0000:00/0000:00:0b.1/usb2/2-2/2-2.3/2-2.3:1.0/input/input9
[ 45.478030] input: Wacom ISDv4 93 as /devices/pci0000:00/0000:00:0b.1/usb2/2-2/2-2.3/2-2.3:1.1/input/input10
```


now do:

```
ls -l /dev/input/by-path
```

That should give you something similar to:


```
lrwxrwxrwx 1 root root 9 2008-07-27 12:07 pci-0000:00:0b.1-usb-0:2.3:1.0-event-mouse -> ../event9
lrwxrwxrwx 1 root root 9 2008-07-27 12:07 pci-0000:00:0b.1-usb-0:2.3:1.0-mouse -> ../mouse1
lrwxrwxrwx 1 root root 9 2008-07-27 12:07 pci-0000:00:0b.1-usb-0:2.3:1.1- -> ../mouse2
lrwxrwxrwx 1 root root 10 2008-07-27 12:07 pci-0000:00:0b.1-usb-0:2.3:1.1-event- -> ../event10
lrwxrwxrwx 1 root root 9 2008-07-27 12:07 platform-i8042-serio-0-event-kbd -> ../event1
lrwxrwxrwx 1 root root 10 2008-07-27 12:07 platform-i8042-serio-1-event-mouse -> ../event11
lrwxrwxrwx 1 root root 9 2008-07-27 12:07 platform-i8042-serio-1-mouse -> ../mouse3
lrwxrwxrwx 1 root root 9 2008-07-27 12:07 platform-pcspkr-event-spkr -> ../event2
```


Now find the file that matches the output of dmesg i.e:

input9 (from dmesg) matches with event9 (in the ls command) So The File

pci-0000:00:0b.1-usb-0:2.3:1.0-event-mouse

is one that we need.

next input10 (from dmesg) matches with event10 (in the ls command) So The File

pci-0000:00:0b.1-usb-0:2.3:1.1-event-

is the other we need.

Now just amend your xorg.conf with those two names that you just got. The one ending with "mouse" should be in the stylus and eraser sections
and the one ending in "event-" should be in the touch section.
In theory since we have the same basic laptops these files should be the same as mine but you need to check....
If you have anything other than a tx2000 it probably will be different.

And that should be it.
Press Ctrl + Alt + Backspace to restart the xserver.

Login and we will now calibrate.

Just open up a terminal and do:

```
wacomcpl
```

A gui!!!! everything you will probably ever need to do with wacom is here. Just read the buttons :)

To make the wacomcpl settings stay after you reboot you need to:

```
chmod +x ~/.xinitrc
```

Then go to System->Preferences->Session

click on add and for the command write "~/.xinitrc" (without the quotes) title it whatever.....

This will only work for the user though. So before you log in it is still uncalibrated.

So to make it system wide (if that is what you want) here is a short how-to:

First do:
```
rm ~.xinitrc
```
Now go into wacomcpl and make it how you want it. (calibrate included)

Now open up .xinitrc and xorg.conf:

```
gedit ~/.xinitrc & gksudo gedit /etc/X11/xorg.conf
```

now you just transfer the stuff over to the xorg.conf.

For example the line in my .xinitrc is:

xsetwacom set touch bottomy "3951"

if you open up a terminal you can use xsetwacom to figure out how to translate it to the xorg.conf.

so what you would do for the line above is:

```
xsetwacom -x get touch bottomy
```
the x stands for xconf.. get obviously gives you the value.

that command outputs

Option	"BottomY"	"3951"

which I would put in my xorg.conf under the touch section.

Here is another short example.

.xinitrc:

xsetwacom set stylus Button3 "Button 3"

command:

```
xsetwacom -x get stylus button3
```

part to put in xorg.conf

	Option	"Button3"	"BUTTON 3"


that's about all there is to it. Hopefully I got across some understanding in there :)

I hope this helps everyone. If you have any problems just post them here and I will help as soon as I can.

Kory

### Post by ztidwell on 2008-07-27
> **gali98 said:**
> 
the pressure on the pen is inverted halfway through, doing weird things (just use gimp to see what I mean)
Kory


I experienced this bug as well.  Using [this]("http://sourceforge.net/tracker/?group_id=69596&atid=525124") bug report as a starting point, I was able to come up with a fix.  Attached is a patch that should be applied to src/xdrv/xf86WacomDefs.h in linuxwacom-0.8.1-1.

Just apply the patch, recompile the driver and then reinstall it.  Once you restart X, the pressure should work correctly.

Just note this was a really quick hack and could easily have unintended side effects (although I haven't noticed any).  If you notice anything weird after you try this, you should probably undo these changes and wait for someone who actually knows what they are doing to fix the issue.

---

### Post by gali98 on 2008-07-28
Aha! I have discovered my error!
There is an important step I forgot.
Actually there is a couple of things that I am going to include.

first just for the sake of it.. reboot if you have not already....

Second we need to make sure you have the current kernel headers.... 
If you are on the generic kernel (default)

then do:

>sudo apt-get install linux-headers-generic

I have the rt kernel so I did:

>sudo apt-get install linux-headers-rt

If you don't know run:

>uname -r

Okay now run

./configure --enable-wacom

then 

>make

 I believe you can safely ignore the warnings about the modules not being built.

Now do 

>sudo make install

Now for the commands I think matter.....

>sudo rmmod wacom (may fail.. thats okay)

>sudo cp ./src/2.6.24/wacom.ko /lib/modules/`uname -r`/kernel/drivers/input/tablet

That should copy the driver over. I think this was the problem.

>sudo depmod -e

>sudo modprobe wacom

at this point try the tablet and touch and it should move stuff around.. just play with it.... 

If still no dice, do ./configure --enable-wacom make and sudo make install and copy the output of all those commands.......

Okay guys try that and if it works let me know and continue on and I will also update the tutorial...

And thanks for that patch ztidwell... I am about to try it out...

Hope this works!
Kory

If you could also tell me how new to ubuntu you are and how much do you understand what you are doing (following this tutorial)... :)

### Post by gali98 on 2008-07-28
Rats!!!!  Ztidwell I did everything I could with your patch but it didn't help...
Actually I can't tell every difference...
Also to which bug report are you refering.... ? the link points to the whole list.

I don't see any on there that appy to my problem.

Here is a more in depth description..

Okay we will have h_pressure = human pressure (how hard I am pressing); max 255

and c_pressure = Computer pressure (how hard the computer sees I am pressing); also max 255

now as h_pressure goes up c_pressure matches up ( i.e 1 for 1, 47 for 47 etc..) until h_pressure reaches ~125 (it looks like at exactly halfway pressure but I am using xidump so it is hard to tell)
then c_pressure jumps up to 255 so that h_pressure(125) = c_pressure(255)

Now as h_pressure continues to increase, c_pressure decrease inversely
so that when h_pressure reaches its max of 255, c_pressure is back down to about 125...


to put this is graphical terms,
When I use gimp and hit halfway pressure the opacity jumps to full opacity.
When I press harder than halfway, the opacity goes down (it should go up)
So bascially I have humpy line that look like earthworms.... :P

That is the best way I can put it...
Also the patch you gave me patches xf86wacomdefs right? But I am using xorg.. doesn't xf86 refer to the other xserver out there? (I have to admit I don't know too much about that....)
I looked through all the source looking for things related to pressure, but I'm kinda lost. (I have a kindergarten degree in programming...)
Needless to say if anyone could help it would be appreciated.....
Ping who works on linux-wacom knows about this now (I told him on the mailing lists)

Also I forgot to address you xyexz...
I know y'all got it working on the .7 series, but take a look at this (near the bottom)
[http://www.nabble.com/Wacom-tablet-USB-touchscreen-on-HP-TX2130ea-td18059563.html](http://www.nabble.com/Wacom-tablet-USB-touchscreen-on-HP-TX2130ea-td18059563.html)

basically ping talks about how he is rewriting the protocol. Apparently the old way was more of a hack, and this is a lot cleaner....
I'm not sure, but there is a reason they are rewriting this. It seems the two latest releases have been totally for USB tablet pc's....
You can use the old way, but I thought I would figure it out on 0.8.1
Mainly just a matter of preference... thanks for the post though :)
Kory

### Post by thegnark on 2008-07-30
So this worked for me, but for some strange reason, my screen reverted back to a generic VGA driver and stuck my in 800x600. Tried rebooting and even reverting to my original xorg.conf... Finally I decided to use the Hardware Drivers Manager to remove and re-add fglrx... no reboot in between. After re-enabling, I rebooted with my original xorg.conf and noted that the login screen looked correct. Moved over to tty1 and replaced xorg.conf with my tablet-enabled version. Moved back over to tty7 hit Ctrl+Alt+Backspace and everything worked - including digitizer!

Strange... but I'l update the guide with a link here and a quick note on the subject.

---

### Post by Felipe_U on 2008-08-07
Hi there, I just installed Hardy 64bit on a tx2032, I got the touchscreen working when I use my fingers, I guess this is the touch config in xorg. ### Post by gali98 on 2008-08-08
Wow lots of questions :)
okay onscreen keyboard

>sudo apt-get install cellwriter

this has a built in keyboard and a handwriting to text thingie.... I like it.

on the rotation I will add that to the tutorial soon... hopefully today but I said that two days ago... :)
If you want an early start here is where I learned how... (This is also the place to learn the buttons):
[http://mirosol.kapsi.fi/tx2020/tx2000howto.htm](http://mirosol.kapsi.fi/tx2020/tx2000howto.htm)
it has a lot of useful stuff, but the suspend and hibernate never worked for me.

In gimp if you select the eraser with the eraser end and paint with the cursor end they should go back and forth. (sometimes you have to do it a couple times.)
But this will only work if you have configured the devices in Gimp (which if you have pressure then they are configured right...)
Kory

### Post by gali98 on 2008-08-09
I am actually working on that now!
If you put 

options snd-hda-intel index=0 model=3stack position_fix=0 single_cmd=0

in /etc/modprobe.d/alsa-base
 then it gets everything working, but it seems a dirty way of doing it. I am going to figure out how to get it workin almost perfect, but it may take some time.
Using that line is what got most everything working, but the mic has a lot of static which I don't think should be there. It also has a lot of extra devices that don't need to be there. On the gimp thing....
upload a copy of xorg.conf (just rename it to xorg.txt so it will upload) and I will take a look to get all that working...
Kory

:guitar:Thanx to you dude, the next time I run vista it will be on a virtual machine.  How do I pay you?

A few bugs I noticed.
The rotate works well except the configurations does note rotate i.e when i rotate 180degrees going (with stylus) left take me right and going up takes me down, I copied ur rotate.sh and counter checked xorg.conf as well as Xmodmap.

TIP

The sound on tx2000 I noticed there are two ways to make it work, one leaves the mute button orange and one turns it blue.  Thats not the only difference one method does work with headphones and one does so I will recommend people to use the following line because it works with headphones the way it suppose to work.

go to /etc/modprobe.d/alsa-base
>sudo gedit /etc/modprobe.d/alsa-base

then as the last line add this entry in a new line paste: 

options snd-hda-intel model=hp

This gives you sound on both spleakers and when you plug in the headphones it mutes the speakers.  External Mic also works perfectly I just finished a skype video/audio call this second.

DO NOT use
 "options snd-hda-intel index=0 model=3stack position_fix=0 single_cmd=0"

on HP tx2000 running hardy 64bit because you will not have sound through the head phones.

cheers

### Post by gali98 on 2008-08-18
Ooo good deal... 

Okay this will remove the kernel driver:

>sudo rm /lib/modules/`uname -r`/kernel/drivers/input/tablet/wacom.ko

The easiest way to remove everything else is to run 
the uninstall.sh script that comes in the prebuilt folder of the linux-wacom folder.

another way (though a little redundent)
is to install the real packages for them then remove them i.e

go to synaptic and search for wacom. Two packages should show up.
install them then apply.
Now right click on them and select remove completely.
That should also work :)

I am about to update the tutorial so you will not have to patch it anymore
yay! :)

Also for now I would leave your xorg.conf alone...
If you feel the need to fix it, make sure to back it up!

>cp /etc/X11/xorg.conf /etc/X11/xorg.conf.bak

Also for you and anyone else using my tutorial... You need to update your xorg.conf file to match mine that is uploaded here. It fixes a few things...
anyway cheers and hope this helps!

Kory

btw: the wacom files are not that big and really don't clutter anything, but I understand where you are coming from. I am way too CDO (OCD in alphabetical order)
:P

> LD [M]  /home/thomas/Desktop/linuxwacom-0.8.1-3/src/2.6.24/wacom.ko

It is definately being built.
check the command. Also you have to run that command 
(sudo cp ./src/2.6.24/wacom.ko /lib/modules/`uname -r`/kernel/drivers/input/tablet) while in the root of the linuxwacom folder.
if you run

>cp /home/thomas/Desktop/linuxwacom-0.8.1-3/src/2.6.24/wacom.ko /lib/modules/`uname -r`/kernel/drivers/input/tablet

it should also work.

### Post by gali98 on 2008-08-24
yes sir that would be the problem ;)
okay in a terminal cd into the root of the linux wacom folder you extracted.

and do these commands:

>./configure --enable-wacom

>make

>sudo make install 

>sudo cp ./src/2.6.24/wacom.ko /lib/modules/`uname -r`/kernel/drivers/input/tablet

>sudo modprobe wacom

now if it still doesn't work... Paste the contents of the terminal (just copy and paste all the output in gnome-terminal) into a text file and upload. The content will be lengthy and we don't want to make a really long post :)

Do that and we can figure out the problem.

Kory

### Post by gali98 on 2008-08-26
Oh my goodness I'm dumb.

I just now realized that you did:

>ls /dev/input/by-path

you need to do

>ls -l /dev/input/by-path

I'm sorry I sent us on a goose chase. I forgot what your original problem was :)

Kory

### Post by gali98 on 2008-08-28
Okay..

First I'm sorry I did not clarify...
Do not worry about .xinitrc   
If it is empty (or not there) it is not a bad thing.

the other error is normal since you have never installed linux-wacom before.
So you don't have to worry about that either.

Okay so now that we got that out of the way, here is what I want you to do..

First delete the old linux wacom folder (the one that was extracted)

now open a brand new terminal and do these commands then if you still get no movement from anything after you restart x (you don't actually have to restart the computer. Just press ctl+alt+backspace) from the touch/stylus then post all the output from the terminal. Just copy it all to a text file and save it before you restart x so you won't lose it all :)

>cd ./Desktop

>wget http://prdownloads.sourceforge.net/linuxwacom/linuxwacom-0.8.1-3.tar.bz2

>tar xjvf linuxwacom-0.8.1-3.tar.bz2

>cd linuxwacom-0.8.1-3

>./configure --enable-wacom

>make

>sudo make install

>sudo cp ./src/2.6.24/wacom.ko /lib/modules/`uname -r`/kernel/drivers/input/tablet/wacom.ko

(that is one line. Just copy and paste)

>sudo rmmod wacom

>sudo depmod -e

>sudo modprobe wacom


you should actually get some random movement from touch/stylus before you even restart x after you load the module. Anyway try all that then if it works follow through with the tutorial. If you hit a snag, just upload that file with all the stuff in it :)

Cheers,
Kory

Some things maybe you think I should add?

Just wanted to improve it so everybody can use it easily. Thanks,
Kory

### Post by gali98 on 2008-08-29
Okay lets just start over....
First of all I noticed you were doing this all as root.
For precision's sake lets do these commands as a normal user (i.e. zimmerman)

First open a spankin' new terminal and do these commands:

>cd ./Desktop

>wget http://prdownloads.sourceforge.net/linuxwacom/linuxwacom-0.8.1-3.tar.bz2

>tar xjvf linuxwacom-0.8.1-3.tar.bz2

>cd linuxwacom-0.8.1-3

>./configure --enable-wacom

>make

>sudo make install

>sudo cp /home/zimmerman/Desktop/linuxwacom-0.8.1-3/src/2.6.24/wacom.ko /lib/modules/2.6.24-19-generic/kernel/drivers/input/tablet/wacom.ko

(that is one line.. just copy and paste.)

>sudo rmmod wacom

>sudo depmod -e

>sudo modprobe wacom

If that does not work then post all the output from the above commands....
Kory

### Post by harak on 2008-08-30
I have a tx2500 

Option "Device" "/dev/input/by-path/pci-0000:00:0b.1-usb-0:2.3:1.1-event-"

in the touch section did not work for me.

Instead, I replaced it with(borrowed from [http://mirosol.kapsi.fi/tx2020/tx2000howto.htm](http://mirosol.kapsi.fi/tx2020/tx2000howto.htm))

Option "Device" "/dev/input/wacom"

But the X Y values are to be same as in gali98's post ([http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?p=5469447#post5469447](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?p=5469447#post5469447))

I used the same settings for stylus and erasor, including X Y values, as in ( [http://mirosol.kapsi.fi/tx2020/tx2000howto.htm](http://mirosol.kapsi.fi/tx2020/tx2000howto.htm))




hope it is helpful to someone

***EDIT***
Sorry Guys that was without fglrx installed (Obviously the laptop will have wrong screen resolutions). Plus I had modified the xorg.conf in ( [http://mirosol.kapsi.fi/tx2020/tx2000howto.htm](http://mirosol.kapsi.fi/tx2020/tx2000howto.htm)). It has a small error. I am attaching my xorg.conf(see immediately next to this message). The Topx yada yada values still need a bit of tweaking, but I am almost there. You can try and send me the optimum values you found. I would also like to add that I to ran the following code before using Kory's ( or gali98's) Tutorial :
sudo update
sudo dist-upgrade

Also, I had selected all kinds of updates in Synaptic (Adept).


Kory (or gali98 ), I did not use any special method other than mentioned above. I started with Kubuntu-kde4 though. For installing Kubuntu, I used this ([http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=873188](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=873188)).  I have tested with Ubuntu as well and it works.Sorry that I could not reply your message as I have not posted 75 times yet


***Edit*** 
One important thing that I would like to mention. The eraser using my settings does not funtion as an eraser. It act like another stylus tip. Hope some one can come with a solution.

My xorg.conf (I mean the touch) does not work properly when I have vnc-java installed.

### Post by gali98 on 2008-08-30
Well if you want to do it now, you can edit the values topx bottomx topy and bottomy in xorg.conf.

However if you wait maybe a few days, another release fo linux wacom will come out where you can calibrate with wacomcpl (the gui)
I have helped test a dev version, and so far the stylus calibration works perfect, but I don't think Ping (the dev) has fixed touch calibration....

As soon as 0.8.1-4 comes out I will update it...

Now onto our ongoing problem.

Guys I really can't figure out the problem....

could you make sure the wacom module is loaded?

lsmod|grep wacom

also do 

dmesg|grep wacom

also could each of you run

wacomcpl

and see if anything shows up (error messages, etc..)

also please upload your current xorg.conf

I know other tx2500 users have gotten this to work.

I'm sorry I can't make this work :(

Kory

### Post by Ununtu on 2008-08-31
YEAH, it's working!

The other bugs were indeed the source of the problem. I managed to correct them (they were coming from the way the old version TX2500 Tutorial was written, it could be mistranslated, and i mistranslated:@ but while translating the new version, I saw my mistake and corrected it)
I then followed Kory's tutorial, and it just work (just need to calibrate it, but I had to tell you first)

I'm REALLY REALLY SORRY for making you look for the bug, you've been very patient with me on this one.
Big thanks for your help and your work, really doing a great job!

Sorry again, mostly to you Kory.

I'll stay tuned to this thread for any new improvements, to put them on the french wiki (don't worry, I've already corrected the translation)

### Post by gali98 on 2008-08-31
I'm just glad you got it working (YAY!!!)
Man, that was frustrating cause I couldn't find where I messed up :P
Don't be sorry at all. We got it working! If you could, describe the error you were talking about as it may be the same error that zoomy942 had.
In fact I may put it in my tutorial...

Also check sometime back this week as 0.8.1-4 is supposed to have calibraton in a gui (click this box then click that box and you're done :)).
Ping (the dev) gave me a dev version to test and at that point the stylus calibration was perfect. The touch was still messed up. That was thursday or Friday and so it should be soon. cross your fingers. That would take a nice bite out of the tutorial also which would be nice.

Also here are some things you might want to check out once you get the calibration right:

Firefox addons: 
Grab and Drag (I love this one) 
All in one gestures (has a LOT of features... but mostly for the stylus)

Apps:
Cellwriter (a great app. use it a lot)
Florence (a good keyboard, but in early stages)
Dasher (okay not too useable, but fun to play with)
System->Preferences->accesiblilty

turn it on.

then go to System->preferences->mouse and go to the accesiblilty tab.

Here you can set it that a double click happens when you hold down your finger or the stylus long enough (like in Vista). I use that a lot.

Anyway have fun!
If you have any questions just post or pm me (I would rather you post if you could though, as then everyone benefits:))

Kory

### Post by harak on 2008-09-01
Hi Kory,
      Thanks for the corrections. I do not know what you mean by the old way. Yours was the first tutorial I used. But the touch was not working well. The cursor did not move with my finger-touch. Then I changed my xorg.conf (probably the old way). The cursor followed my fingers. I haven't tested other functionalities.

In windows the back of the pen acts as an eraser in Microsoft Journal. I thought it should be same when I use Xournal or Gournal in Linux. I realise that its the side button on the pen that acts as an eraser.

---

### Post by gali98 on 2008-09-01
Right. It is the program that delegates what end does which. The wacom driver just sends it as a button press with some extra stuff (pressure, etc...) and it is up to the program how to interpret it. I wish gournal, etc. would know you were using the eraser end, but I guess not. Maybe after those programs mature a little more...
Kory

---

### Post by martinjochimsen on 2008-09-01
Thanks gali98 for the FANTASTIC update. I finally got everything to work!!! Even the calibration worked out-the-box - actually better than in my Vista.
Maybe it would have worked before, but I didn't understand the part with


"Now find the file that matches the output of dmesg i.e:
input9 (from dmesg) matches with event9 (in the ls command) So The File
pci-0000:00:0b.1-usb-0:2.3:1.0-event-mouse
is one that we need.
next input10 (from dmesg) matches with event10 (in the ls command) So The File
pci-0000:00:0b.1-usb-0:2.3:1.1-event-
is the other we need.
Now just amend your xorg.conf with those two names that you just got. The one ending with "mouse" should be in the stylus and eraser sections
and the one ending in "event-" should be in the touch section."

Especially the "amend"-part I didn't understand, but I keept cool this time, and didn't just copy/paste with my eyes closed!!! :-D

By the way I got a tx2590oe.

Best regards
Martin Jochimsen .-)

### Post by gali98 on 2008-09-02
Okay..
We are now going to go deeper. I got it solved with the other guy so hopefully I can get it done with you.
First are you on a tx2500 series? If so you need to follow this tutorial. I think it has some things you need.
Do First Boot to step 2 then come back here...

[http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=873188](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=873188)

Okay now do these commands and post the output. These commands may seem strange, but they may be needed. I want to cover all bases.

sudo apt-get install wacom-tools xserver-xorg-input-wacom

sudo apt-get purge wacom-tools xserver-xorg-input-wacom

sudo rmmod wacom

sudo rm /lib/modules/`uname -r`/kernel/drivers/input/tablet/wacom.ko

sudo modprobe wacom

lsmod | grep wacom

cd ~/Desktop

Delete any previous linux wacom folder

wget http://prdownloads.sourceforge.net/linuxwacom/linuxwacom-0.8.1-4.tar.bz2

tar xjvf linuxwacom-0.8.1-4.tar.bz2

cd linuxwacom-0.8.1-4

./prebuilt/install

./prebuilt/uninstall

./configure --enable-wacom

make

sudo make install

sudo cp /home/zimmerman/Desktop/linuxwacom-0.8.1-4/src/2.6.24/wacom.ko /lib/modules/`uname -r`/kernel/drivers/input/tablet/wacom.ko

sudo depmod -e

sudo modprobe wacom

lsmod | grep wacom

That should get you going, but post the output of everything anyway. That note you saw is supposed to be there don't worry.
Some of these commands will fail. I made them that way just to check things. Just post everything.
Kory

### Post by gali98 on 2008-09-04
Okay...
Zoomy I uploaded an xorg.conf that should work. That make.conf (or whatever it says) is something you don't have to worry about. It is when you are compiling a kernel which you don't need to do.
Try it and get back to me.

Okay zujenbe:

First I need the model of your laptop....

Now just do every single one of these commands in the terminal then copy and paste all the output here. It would be best if you copied into a text file then uploaded that here.  Do These one at a time!

sudo apt-get update

sudo apt-get install build-essential libx11-dev libxi-dev x11proto-input-dev xserver-xorg-dev tk8.4-dev tcl8.4-dev libncurses5-dev

sudo apt-get upgrade

sudo apt-get install wacom-tools xserver-xorg-input-wacom

sudo apt-get purge wacom-tools xserver-xorg-input-wacom

sudo rmmod wacom

sudo rm /lib/modules/`uname -r`/kernel/drivers/input/tablet/wacom.ko

cd ~/Desktop

****Delete any previous linux wacom folder***

wget http://prdownloads.sourceforge.net/linuxwacom/linuxwacom-0.8.1-4.tar.bz2

tar xjvf linuxwacom-0.8.1-4.tar.bz2

cd linuxwacom-0.8.1-4

./prebuilt/install

./prebuilt/uninstall

./configure --enable-wacom

make

sudo make install

sudo cp ~/Desktop/linuxwacom-0.8.1-4/src/2.6.24/wacom.ko /lib/modules/`uname -r`/kernel/drivers/input/tablet/wacom.ko

sudo depmod -e

sudo modprobe wacom

lsmod | grep wacom


Okay do all that then get back to me.
Kory

---

### Post by gali98 on 2008-09-05
Okay I need you to all the commands.
You skipped a few.
Delete the previous folder.
and do each command exactly as I typed.
Use sudo not su.
It is just easier for me to find the errors that way.
The main one you skipped is the most required:

./configure --enable-wacom

it will not work if you do this. At all......
So please do those commands and post the output :)
Kory

### Post by zujenbe on 2008-09-05
ok so, after all that warranty garbage and bla, 

#ifndef PIXMAN_H__
#define PIXMAN_H__

#include <pixman-version.h>

/*
 * Standard integers
 */
#if defined (__SVR4) && defined (__sun)
#  include <sys/int_types.h>
#  include <stdint.h>
#elif defined (__OpenBSD__)
#  include <inttypes.h>
#elif defined (_MSC_VER)
typedef __int8 int8_t;
typedef unsigned __int8 uint8_t;
typedef __int16 int16_t;
typedef unsigned __int16 uint16_t;
typedef __int32 int32_t;
typedef unsigned __int32 uint32_t;
typedef __int64 int64_t;
typedef unsigned __int64 uint64_t;
#else
 hope this helps

---

### Post by olejorgen on 2008-09-05
I resolved the missing header issue by simply making links to the headers (pixman-version.h and pixman.h) in /usr/include/xorg. Do a search in /usr/include to find them

---

### Post by gali98 on 2008-09-05

zippy do these commands and try make again...

sudo ln -s /usr/include/pixman-1/pixman-version.h /usr/include/xorg/pixman-version.h

Kory

### Post by gali98 on 2008-09-06
Rothariger:

then run nvidia-settings

You can probably set that up there.

Zujenbe (I accidentally called you zippy... I get so confused....:))

### Post by olejorgen on 2008-09-06
You might need to configure gimp to use the stylus. At least I had to do that in inkscape.

Try if you get pressure sensitivity in xournal. (it's an option, so be sure to select it)

---

### Post by gali98 on 2008-09-06
go to file -> preferences

Then look for input devices.

Click configure input devices and it should open a dialog window.
Now there should a dropdown menu that has wacom devices in it (i.e stylus, touch, eraser.)

Now when you click on one of those i.e stylus there is another dropdown box beside it.
Make that screen. Do this for stylus touch and eraser and pressure will work.
Kory

---

### Post by tasism on 2008-09-07
> **gali98 said:**
> go to file -> preferences

Then look for input devices.

Click configure input devices and it should open a dialog window.
Now there should a dropdown menu that has wacom devices in it (i.e stylus, touch, eraser.)

Now when you click on one of those i.e stylus there is another dropdown box beside it.
Make that screen. Do this for stylus touch and eraser and pressure will work.
Kory

Excellent! Thanks Kory, works like a charm.

The only thing that does not work now is the eraser (it works like a pen for some strange reason). Any ideas why this is?

Thanks again, T.

---

### Post by gali98 on 2008-09-07
Yes just select the paintbrush with the stylus, then select the eraser with the eraser end. You may have to do it a couple times, but eventually the tools will stick with the right ends. You can even map the touch to a tool.
(I use smudge just to be cool)

However there is one thing you have to do.

Go back into the devices dialog (the one with "screen" and stuff.)

and select touch.

Now below that there should be a box labeled pressure. Just change that to 4.

Kory

---

### Post by gali98 on 2008-09-09
Kirys, depends...

First, what tablet do you have. If you have a USB Tablet PC (tx2000 or tx2500) then maybe, if you have a normal tablet (bamboo, graphire, etc..) then no.

Second what version of linux wacom are you on. If 0.8.1-4 then no, other version, maybe.

Third By calibration you mean doing the gui calibration.
You can calibrate any version by modifying the xorg.conf.

Finally, if you are on an older version, it is not that hard to upgrade. Most of the work is already done.
Here are all the commands that you should need to do if you are on a USB Tablet PC...

cd ~/Desktop

****Delete any previous linux wacom folder***

wget http://prdownloads.sourceforge.net/linuxwacom/linuxwacom-0.8.1-4.tar.bz2

tar xjvf linuxwacom-0.8.1-4.tar.bz2

cd linuxwacom-0.8.1-4

./prebuilt/uninstall

./configure --enable-wacom

make

sudo make install

sudo cp ~/Desktop/linuxwacom-0.8.1-4/src/2.6.24/wacom.ko /lib/modules/`uname -r`/kernel/drivers/input/tablet/wacom.ko

sudo depmod -e

sudo modprobe wacom

then restart X with ctrl alt backspace.

Then you just run wacomcpl to calibrate and other stuff.



Zoomy, using wacomcpl you can assign what stylus buttons go to what mouse buttons. just select the stylus then click the button about tools (it is the one under Feel. I can't remember what the name of it is.) there you can configure buttons and whatnot.

chikko, I downloaded alpha 5 yesterday, and will try and test it soon. (may not be today though) I think my email on the list might not have made it. I will have to check at home...

Kory

---

It's like if I had both mode (calibrated and uncalibrated) active at the same time!.

For calibration I use the script produced by wacomcpl
```
xsetwacom set eraser bottomx "26327"
xsetwacom set eraser bottomy "16599"
xsetwacom set eraser bottomx "26255"
xsetwacom set eraser topy "119"
xsetwacom set eraser topx "-2"
xsetwacom set stylus bottomy "16599"
xsetwacom set stylus bottomx "26255"
xsetwacom set stylus topy "119"
xsetwacom set stylus topx "-2"

```

Bye

### Post by gali98 on 2008-09-11
hmmmm.... okay here is what you're going to have to do.

cd into the linuxwacom folder on your Desktop...

then do ./configure --enable-wacom --prefix=/usr/local/

then do 

make

and finally

sudo make install..

Then run wacomcpl again.

this won't touch your xorg.conf which is what I think you had the most trouble....

Kory

Edit: I tried to get the 2.6.27 kernel and I could not.

The dev at linuxwacom knows, but it may be a week or two before he gets to it :(

### Post by M42 on 2008-09-19
> **kirys said:**
> Well calibration works but have some side effects
after calibration drawing quality is much worse.
Look at the attached image the upper line is before calibration and the lower one after, 
The first is smooth while the other is rough, is a known side effect or a bug of the driver?
[IMG]http://ubuntuforums.org/attachment.php?attachmentid=84703&d=1220978625[/IMG]

I had this problem as well.  Someone, don't recall who, came up with a fix that worked for me.  The fix is to go to the linuxwacom folder and edit the config.status file by eliminating or commenting out (this is what I did) the two line that refer to TABLET_SCALING.  Then re-run Kory's guide AFTER the line ./configure --enable-wacom

Now Xjournal lines are great.  Hope this helps.

### Post by gali98 on 2008-09-21
Java is not a requirement....
I don't want to put uneeded packages into the tutorial, especially since Sun Java is not totally free (as in freedom).
I actaully posted a reply to you M2, but apparently it did not go through.
Thanks for the comments and fixes! On the second post, in my tutorial it installs tcl/tk...

I plan to, in my next version of the tutorial, Put a troubleshooting section with help with the problems like above. In the meantime I suggest if you are having libwacomcfg problems, you first try,
./configure --enable-wacom --prefix=/usr/local/
make 
sudo make install

and if you still get the same error do:

./configure --enable-wacom --prefix=/usr/
make 
sudo make install

Studbucket... No my tutorial does not cover rotating. However when 0.8.1-5  comes out I will add it.
In the meantime here is a preview.
there is a tar.gz package with three files in it below. Download that and extract the three files onto the Desktop.
Copy Xmodmap and rotation.sh to your home folder

Then rename them with a . in front of them (.Xmodmap and .rotation.sh)

now open up a terminal and do the following commands...

cd ~/Desktop
gcc -lX11 -lXrandr -o rotation rotate.c
now on your desktop you will find a file named rotation.
copy that to your home folder and name it .rotation.bin
Okay now go to System->Preferences->Sessions

and click add. For name put rotation. For command put
~/.rotation.bin

click okay and exit out. Now open a terminal and run gconf-editor

go to apps->metacity->global_keybindings
on the right find run_command_1 and double click it.
For the value put 
XF86Launch0

Now go to keybinding_commands (under global_keybindings)
and double click on command_1 and make the value
sh ~/.rotation.sh
Now close out of everything and restart x (ctl alt backspace)
When you log in, a box will come up talking about xmodmap. Basically you need to load the file that is on the right over to the left.
Now just click the quickplay button on the laptop (the one under the dvd button) and the screen (with tablet and touch) will rotate. 

This will probably only work on the tx2000 series. All you have to do is run xev to find the keycode of whatever key you want to use to rotate then edit ~/.Xmodmap with that keycode. 
By the way, I did not write the rotate program or the script, I just modded them so that they work for us. When I add it to the main tutorial I will give credit where is due.

If you have problems, post back...
Kory

---

### Post by gali98 on 2008-10-19
Okay run that command as it actually appears (use the `)
But just so you know, those aren't quotes. Or apostrophes. Not sure of the actual name, but it is above the tilde(~) key (i.e if you do shift+tilde).
The easiest way to do the command though is to triple click on the command (that will select it all) then go to the terminal and press ctrl+shift+v.
That will leave no room for mistakes.
Kory

p.s. You could substitute your own uname -r, but what the `s do is output that straight in the command. Either way it will work.

### Post by gali98 on 2008-10-20
Okay I am back... :)

The whole wacom install has very little files (less than twenty total) and they are all very small.
In fact running those commands over and over again will not increase the number of files in your system, they will simply overwrite them.
For what exactly the commands do:

the configure command gets the compiler ready to compile the source. It adds makefiles with options such as what kernel to compile for, and to compile the kernel module for wacom. 
the make command actually compiles the source that was configured with the above command.
the sudo make install command installs those compiled files into the system. (compiling just leaves them in the same directory as the source.) the sudo part gives you root access, because you need that to put the files in all the right places.
finally that big long command that begins with "cp" copies the kernel module to the right place because the sudo make install command does not do that part for us.

Do not worry about stranded files and such. If you are that worried, you can go into the linuxwacom directory and do either two things. Run "sudo prebuilt/uninstall"
and that will remove all the wacom files from your system.


Now onto your problem...
You probably need to run the configure command like so:
./configure --enable-wacom --prefix=/usr

then run
make
sudo make install 
sudo cp ./src/2.6.24/wacom.ko /lib/modules/`uname -r`/kernel/drivers/input/tablet/wacom.ko

then restart and see if wacomcpl starts. If it does still not work, 
please run the following command
strace xsetwacom
and post the output.
Thanks, 
Kory
@steve I am about to test the codec. The main thing I am hoping for is for the mic to work (front mic) but I am not holding my breath.

### Post by kirys on 2008-10-25
> **gali98 said:**
> Hmmm... so you installed java and it worked?
Kory

I discovered the reason!
as you remember the default instal location of wacom tools is:
/usr/local

this means that the wacom libs will be installed into '/usr/local/lib' that is not into the lib search path (by default).
When sun java is installed the installer adds '/usr/local/lib' to the lib search path and this does the trick.

So there are two ways of solve this:
add --prefix=/usr/ to the configure command
add '/usr/local/lib' to the lib search path

Cya

### Post by gali98 on 2008-10-26
The instructions are a bit muddled because there's a lot of information to cover, and it is in sort of a transition between Hardy and Intrepid.

Basically you should run the configure, make, make install, then the cp command (the really long command that copies the modules)
After that restart. However after that you could restart at any point after you run those first commands. (i.e. you could go on and configure your xorg.conf and run the modprobe commands....)
if you are still having problems, run all these commands over again: (just cd into the linuxwacom folder)

./configure --enable-wacom --prefix=/usr

make

sudo make install

Now if you are on Hardy (8.04) run:
sudo cp ./src/2.6.24/wacom.ko /lib/modules/`uname -r`/kernel/drivers/input/tablet/wacom.ko
and if you are on Intrepid (8.10) run:
sudo cp ./src/2.6.27/wacom.ko /lib/modules/`uname -r`/kernel/drivers/input/tablet/wacom.ko
(really you could run both just to be sure. One just won't work and won't cause any problems.)

Now restart and it should work. 
****it won't be calibrated. You can move the cursor, but very oddly and only in certain places on the screen. Try all parts of the screen.

If you can't get any movement at all, post the output of:
sudo lsusb -vvv

and

sudo dmesg|grep Wacom


@cardude
Glad to help!
Kory

### Post by TheBernok on 2008-11-01
I am on Intrepid, tx2500z, fresh install.

After doing 
```
tar xjvf linuxwacom-0.8.1-6.tar.bz2

cd linuxwacom-0.8.1-6

./configure --enable-wacom

make

sudo make install

sudo rmmod wacom

sudo cp ./src/2.6.27/wacom.ko /lib/modules/`uname -r`/kernel/drivers/input/tablet/wacom.ko

sudo depmod -e

sudo modprobe wacom
```

The cursor does not move with either the eraser, pen or touch.

### Post by gali98 on 2008-11-02
First...
@jcm1979

Look in your xorg.conf.... under the stylus section, there is a line that says:
	Option "Button2" "3"

comment that out (and save it) then restart X (ctrl+alt+backspace) 
and see if that fixs it... If not, then delete /home/yourusername/.xinitrc
and that should fix it...(restart x again)


Now onto  th89...
I think the problem has to do with the way Intrepid normally handles wacom devices..
Here is what I want you to try...

sudo apt-get install wacom-tools xserver-xorg-input-wacom
sudo apt-get purge wacom-tools xserver-xorg-input-wacom

Now you will need to install everything again... so cd into the linux wacom folder and do
 sudo prebuilt/uninstall (to get rid of everything)

./configure --enable-wacom

make

sudo make install

sudo cp ./src/2.6.27/wacom.ko /lib/modules/`uname -r`/kernel/drivers/input/tablet/wacom.ko

Your xorg.conf is good, so you should just have to restart to get it working.... You may need to restart more than once (don't ask me why.. I had to restart like 3 times)
and open wacomcpl up to see if everything shows up in there.

Finally, TheBernok

your problem is your xorg.conf...
I am uploading the one you need. Just copy and paste it into your existing one and restart and see what happens...
Have fun guys..
Kory

---

There it is with "sudo make install" unfortunately still no touch and no tablet.

I think I read somewhere right before downloading Intrepid that Intrepid does not use the xorg.conf for input devices or something.  It was just something I saw in passing and since I am no expert I just let it go by and don't even remember the source.  However my xorg.conf being so dissimilar to what it was in hardy has left me wondering.  I tried adding all the proper sections and now I am in low graphics mode. :/  So I will restore the old one...

Edit:  From the Ubuntu 8.10 release notes:

[I]X.Org Input Devices

The X.Org configuration file (/etc/X11/xorg.conf) still has InputDevice entries for the mouse and keyboard, but they are ignored now because input-hotplug is used. The keyboard settings now come from /etc/default/console-setup; to change them please use sudo dpkg-reconfigure console-setup. After that, HAL and X need to be restarted (e.g., by rebooting your system).
X.Org evdev xmodmap incompatibility

The X keycodes generated with the new evdev input driver in X.Org 1.5 are not compatible with those generated in Ubuntu 8.04 LTS and before. If you have configured keybindings for your user with a ~/.Xmodmap file, you will need to convert or disable it by hand on upgrade. [/I]

Could these things potentially have to do with my anemic xorg.conf and the fact that the tablet input is not working no matter how many times I run through the tutorial?

Edit 2:
This bug report sends me in a totally different direction and mentions how editing the xorg like we are attempting will cause X not to load in Intrepid (Which I think is why I had that graphics issue and had to restore mine.)
[https://bugs.launchpad.net/ubuntu/+source/wacom-tools/+bug/282203](https://bugs.launchpad.net/ubuntu/+source/wacom-tools/+bug/282203)
I will keep butting my head against it till it works of course, but if anyone has any specific advice I would appreciate it. :)

---

### Post by Murphy2712 on 2008-11-03
I think you also need to do :
sudo cp src/2.6.27/wacom.ko /lib/modules/`uname -r`/kernel/drivers/input/tablet/
between "sudo rmmod wacom" and "sudo modprobe wacom".

What are your results of "dmesg |grep Wacom", "ls -l /dev/input/by-path/" and "cat /var/log/Xorg.0.log |grep EE" ?

---

### Post by Murphy2712 on 2008-11-03
If your xorg.conf is this empty it's normal that your tablet doesn't respond : you need to configure it :)

There's some strange lines here :
```
[   13.430762] input: Wacom ISDv4 93 as /devices/pci0000:00/0000:00:0b.1/usb2/2-2/2-2.3/2-2.3:1.0/input/input10
[   13.495240] input: Wacom ISDv4 93 as /devices/pci0000:00/0000:00:0b.1/usb2/2-2/2-2.3/2-2.3:1.1/input/input11
[   13.545375] wacom: v1.49:USB Wacom Graphire and Wacom Intuos tablet driver
[ 1859.296854] input: Wacom ISDv4 93 as /devices/pci0000:00/0000:00:0b.1/usb2/2-2/2-2.3/2-2.3:1.0/input/input13
[ 1859.331803] input: Wacom ISDv4 93 as /devices/pci0000:00/0000:00:0b.1/usb2/2-2/2-2.3/2-2.3:1.1/input/input14
[ 1859.369298] wacom: v1.49:USB Wacom Graphire and Wacom Intuos tablet driver

```
Your Wacom is detected but not in the same input at time 13 and at time 1859 (maybe because of the new driver you just compile).
So the last time we have input13 and input14.
It corresponds with ... nothing in /dev/input/by-path/ !
Could you reboot and repost "dmesg |grep Wacom" and "ls -l /dev/input/by-path/" ?

### Post by vitreoushumours on 2008-11-03
I went rogue and using the steps at 
[https://help.ubuntu.com/community/Wacom](https://help.ubuntu.com/community/Wacom)
and at:
[https://help.ubuntu.com/community/WacomTroubleshooting](https://help.ubuntu.com/community/WacomTroubleshooting)
I ended up installing the older 8.1.4 wacom tools and utilities, and then edited my xorg as they suggested...I now have movement but of course there is no touchscreen and the pen is horribly un-calibrated...the wacomcpl does not even work to calibrate it.  (It completely fails to recognize the click.)  The bonus thing is, that now I have a "Server layout" and some of the correct sections in my xorg.conf and it did not hose my graphics...the unfortunate thing is that now I guess I need to start over from square one in this thread.

I will post those results as soon as I have done so.

### Post by vitreoushumours on 2008-11-03
RESOLVED!!!

So I guess my whole problem was simply that in Intrepid if you do a fresh install instead of an upgrade, your xorg.conf file is almost empty because intrepid uses another method for the touchpad and some other devices.  This actually makes things easier to a degree because I didn't have to edit the synaptics touchpad and rename it to "pad" as was stated in the original tutorial.

I have the basic tx2000 series so I did not need to change the device input from what was posted in the tutorial (pci-0000:00:0b.1-usb-0:2.3:1.0-event-mouse; and pci-0000:00:0b.1-usb-0:2.3:1.1-event-) worked great for me (event 10 and event 11 in my case.)

Here is what my xorg.conf looks like now.  I am posting it in case anyone else with a fresh install of intrepid wants to copy it, or use it as a reference.

```
# xorg.conf (X.Org X Window System server configuration file)
#
# This file was generated by dexconf, the Debian X Configuration tool, using
# values from the debconf database.
#
# Edit this file with caution, and see the xorg.conf manual page.
# (Type "man xorg.conf" at the shell prompt.)
#
# This file is automatically updated on xserver-xorg package upgrades *only*
# if it has not been modified since the last upgrade of the xserver-xorg
# package.
#
# Note that some configuration settings that could be done previously
# in this file, now are automatically configured by the server and settings
# here are ignored.
#
# If you have edited this file but would like it to be automatically updated
# again, run the following command:
#   sudo dpkg-reconfigure -phigh xserver-xorg

Section "Device"
	Identifier	"Configured Video Device"
EndSection

Section "Monitor"
	Identifier	"Configured Monitor"
EndSection

Section "Screen"
	Identifier	"Default Screen"
	Monitor		"Configured Monitor"
	Device		"Configured Video Device"
EndSection

Section "ServerFlags"
        Option "AutoAddDevices" "False"
EndSection

Section "InputDevice"
Identifier "stylus"
Driver "wacom"
Option "Type" "stylus"
Option "USB" "on"
Option "Device" "/dev/input/by-path/pci-0000:00:0b.1-usb-0:2.3:1.0-event-mouse"
Option "Button2" "3" # make side-switch a right button
Option "TopX" "225"
Option "TopY" "225"
Option "BottomX" "26300"
Option "BottomY" "16375"
EndSection

Section "InputDevice"
Identifier "touch"
Driver "wacom"
Option "Type" "touch"
Option "USB" "on"
Option "Device" "/dev/input/by-path/pci-0000:00:0b.1-usb-0:2.3:1.1-event-"
Option "TopX" "200"
Option "TopY" "225"
Option "BottomX" "4000"
Option "BottomY" "3875"
EndSection

Section "InputDevice"
Identifier "eraser"
Driver "wacom"
Option "Type" "eraser"
Option "Device" "/dev/input/by-path/pci-0000:00:0b.1-usb-0:2.3:1.0-event-mouse"
Option "USB" "on"
EndSection

Section "ServerLayout"
        Identifier      "Default Layout"
        Screen          "Default Screen"
        Inputdevice "stylus"	"SendCoreEvents"
	Inputdevice "touch"	"SendCoreEvents"
	Inputdevice "eraser"	"SendCoreEvents"
EndSection
``` 

I will probably try commenting out the ServerFlags section since I am not quite sure what it does, and even though it was added at [https://help.ubuntu.com/community/Wacom](https://help.ubuntu.com/community/Wacom) and [https://help.ubuntu.com/community/WacomTroubleshooting](https://help.ubuntu.com/community/WacomTroubleshooting) I am not sure if it really needs to be there.

Thanks for the help, I really appreciate this tutorial and the helpful people in this forum.  Once I figure out how to officially "thank" them I will. :)

---

### Post by Murphy2712 on 2008-11-03

### Post by gali98 on 2008-11-03
Hey guys! Sorry for all the confusion. I have updated the tutorial so hopefully we won't have quite as many problems. With Intrepid it is imperative that you restart after copying the module.
So I basically took out all the modprobe depmod commands because they are worthless at this point since you still have to restart.
@Murphy and vitreoushumours

Glad you got it working!
Just for your info, the reason those wacom devices got created twice is because he unloaded the module then loaded it again. When you do that it scraps the old events and uses new ones, but the log of it is still in dmesg. :)
vitreoushumours just for your info, if you ever need a xorg.conf file and you lose yours, you can simply use mine (the one right below my tutorial)
As long as you are using the nvida graphics driver it will work perfect.
This goes for anyone with a tx2000. If you have a tx2500 this will not work. However I can still help pretty much anyone get their xorg.conf squared away...
Also I think you can comment out that line that you were talking about if you refer to below.. (i.e. I don't have that line and it works fine...)


TO ALL WITH CURSOR DRAG PROBLEMS!!!

Okay.. this is the only thing I can think to do. I am not experiencing this issue at all.
so Run these two commands:

```
sudo apt-get install wacom-tools xserver-xorg-input-wacom
sudo apt-get purge wacom-tools xserver-xorg-input-wacom
```

then cd into the linux wacom folder and run these commands:

```
sudo prebuilt/uninstall (to get rid of everything)

./configure --enable-wacom

make

sudo make install

sudo cp ./src/2.6.27/wacom.ko /lib/modules/`uname -r`/kernel/drivers/input/tablet/wacom.ko
```
Now restart (you don't have to mess with your xorg.conf if you have already configured it. If you have your xorg.conf from Hardy, it should work perfect with Intrepid. Mine does at least :))
See if that works...
I would comment out the lines

```
Section "ServerFlags"
        Option "AutoAddDevices" "False"
EndSection
```
also just to make sure.
I am also uploading my xorg.conf for your convenience for you to check against yours.

If I missed anything please post back and I will try and help again :)
Thanks guys
Kory

### Post by th89 on 2008-11-04
For those wanting to use Xournal in Intrepid. Apparently there is a bug with libgnome canvas, that causes Xournal to be unusable.

> 
Applications which use libgnomecanvas, such as xournal, do not update the screen properly when the user draws lines. Some lines don't appear, others are shown after the cursor moves off the canvas, others are partially displayed and are later completed after releasing the mouse button. This was patched, but did not solve the problem. The updated patch is located [https://bugzilla.novell.com/show_bug.cgi?id=430785](https://bugzilla.novell.com/show_bug.cgi?id=430785) and the debdiff is at [http://launchpadlibrarian.net/19312323/libgnomecanvas_2.20.1.1-1ubuntu3.debdiff](http://launchpadlibrarian.net/19312323/libgnomecanvas_2.20.1.1-1ubuntu3.debdiff)

[https://bugs.launchpad.net/ubuntu/intrepid/+source/libgnomecanvas/+bug/272316](https://bugs.launchpad.net/ubuntu/intrepid/+source/libgnomecanvas/+bug/272316)

I downloaded the source code, downloaded the updated debdiff at the bottom of page, patched the source code, and then rebuilt them into debs. 

To install this patch, just download these debs into the same folder, cd into that folder, and run:
```
sudo dpkg -i libgnomecanvas*.deb
```

This fixed the problem I had with Xournal not working correctly. Before Xournal would be very laggy, would not draw correctly when the window was resized, and other problems. After this patch everything seems to be working correctly as far as I can tell.

I also uploaded the debdiff file I used as well, for those who want it.

---

### Post by th89 on 2008-11-04
Hey all, here's another thing for those of you having problems with rotating screen. Here's what I did:

```
sudo gedit /etc/X11/xorg.conf
```
Then I added the following line under my nvidia driver section:
```
Option  "RandRRotation" "on"
```

```
Section "Device"
	Identifier	"Configured Video Device"
	Driver	"nvidia"
	Option	"NoLogo"	"True"
	Option  "RandRRotation" "on"
EndSection
```

I also made some changes to the rotate code to rotate my cursor. I ran "wacomcpl" in the terminal, and looked for the names of my devices, which happened to be stylus, eraser, and touch. I then edited my rotate script so it had these names in it (I also removed the rotate right, and changed the order in which it rotates, mainly for personal preference). I attached my rotate script below. To use it just rename it to something like ".rotate" and set it to executable. 

Hope this is a help for someone. It woulda saved me some time, for sure.

---

### Post by gali98 on 2008-11-05
@goldenroad

it must not have installed correctly..
please open the terminal and cd into the linux wacom folder then run these commands:

   ```
 make clean
    sudo prebuilt/uninstall 
    ./configure --enable-wacom --prefix=/usr
    make
    sudo make install
    sudo cp src/2.6.24/wacom.ko /lib/modules/`uname -r`/kernel/drivers/input/tablet/
```

then restart and run wacomcpl again. Make sure you run all those commands.



Okay th89, I haven't been able to replicate the problem with the suspend... it just works... maybe an update fixed it ?
anyway thanks for the Help with rotation and xournal :)

to all you who are trying to rotate, and the buttons aren't working (the two bottom ones will not work regardless)
you can make them work by using these two commands:
   ```
 sudo update-rc.d -f hotkey-setup remove 
    sudo update-rc.d hotkey-setup start 99  6 5 4 3 2 1 .

```
You will need to restart afterward...

@mahill and epgui
please upload your xorg.conf and tell me what exact model laptop you have by looking on the bottom.


also to all the rest of you, if you have updated in the last few days and noticed the tablet stopped working, it is because all the modules were replaced, simply recompile and copy the module:

   ```
 
    ./configure --enable-wacom --prefix=/usr
    make
    sudo make install
    sudo cp src/2.6.27/wacom.ko /lib/modules/`uname -r`/kernel/drivers/input/tablet/
```

or if you are still on Hardy:
 ```
sudo cp src/2.6.24/wacom.ko /lib/modules/`uname -r`/kernel/drivers/input/tablet/
```

Hopefully this won't happen too often.
Kory

### Post by th89 on 2008-11-06
@chrono144
Yeah, thats the one you should copy. The 2.6.27-7 is refering to your kernel version. If you were running a previous version of Ubuntu, the folder would be something like /lib/modules/2.6.24.3-generic/kernel/drivers/input/tablet/wacom.k. If the tutorial says somthing different, as far as numbers, that just means it was written for a earlier version of ubuntu.

### Post by gali98 on 2008-11-07
Okay.....
First @a_toff
The reason it is not working is because you have not configured your xorg.conf yet....
I have uploaded the one you need. simply copy and paste it into your present configuration, then restart and see if it works. You may have to restart more than once.

@chrono

If you are getting those errors then you did not run the commands at the beginning of the tutorial.
Please run those, then try and recompile..

sudo apt-get update

sudo apt-get install build-essential libx11-dev libxi-dev x11proto-input-dev xserver-xorg-dev tk8.4-dev tcl8.4-dev libncurses5-dev

sudo apt-get upgrade

sudo apt-get install wacom-tools xserver-xorg-input-wacom

sudo apt-get purge wacom-tools xserver-xorg-input-wacom


@chadmerkert
the reasone everyone elses xorg has stuff in it is because they have already configured it :)
Anyway, I have uploaded your xorg.conf as well, please try it and see what happens...

Also, whenever you make changes to your xorg.conf, always make a backup.. always!
Kory

### Post by Loïc2 on 2008-11-08
> **chadmerkert said:**
> I tried the xorg file you gave me, and when i rebooted it brought me to a command line login, i loged in and tried startx and it gave me this:

Parse error on line 79 of section ServerLayout in file /etc/X11/xorg.conf
      This section must have an Identifier line.
(EE) Problem parsing the config file
(EE) Error parsing the config file

Fatal server error:
no screens found
giving up.
xinit: connection refused (errno 111): unable to connect to X server
xinit: NO such process (errno 3): Server error.

That's the traditionnal error when you edit xorg.conf for wacom tablets on an xorg.conf that didn't have the "ServerLayout" section.

Check the example xorg.conf files at [https://help.ubuntu.com/community/WacomTroubleshooting](https://help.ubuntu.com/community/WacomTroubleshooting) and the guide at [https://help.ubuntu.com/community/Wacom](https://help.ubuntu.com/community/Wacom).

Basically, your ServerLayout section should look like this:

```
Section "ServerLayout"
  Identifier    "Default Layout"
  Screen        "Default Screen"
  InputDevice   "stylus"  "SendCoreEvents"
  InputDevice   "eraser"  "SendCoreEvents"
  InputDevice   "cursor"  "SendCoreEvents" # For non-LCD tablets only
  InputDevice   "pad"                      # For Intuos3/CintiqV5/Graphire4/Bamboo tablets
  InputDevice   "touch"   "SendCoreEvents" # Only a few TabletPCs support this type
EndSection
```

Make sure you have at least the lines for  
```
Identifier    "Default Layout"
Screen        "Default Screen"
```

and edit the rest accordingly (check what Section "InputDevice" you have in your xorg.conf among the stylus, eraser, cursor, pad and touch ones.

If nothing works, make sure you don't have a second screen plugged, make sure you don't have 2 graphic card installed (both can lead to problem with the following command) and type in a console (do CTRL-ALT-F1):
```
sudo dpkg-reconfigure -phigh xserver-xorg
```

### Post by gali98 on 2008-11-08
Glad to help guys!
I figured out why the xorg.conf messed you up.. the very last line was missing an "n"... sorry about that. for that reason, I took down that file. If you ever need it again, you can use the one I am attaching here.
(Thanks Loic for the help!)

Okay
@th89 and chrono

Chrono do not use that link for rotation. You have a tx2500 (we have a tx2000 th89) and you have Ati graphics while we have nvdia. therefore it will not work for that link.
Check this post and see if you can get it to work:
[http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=6089488&postcount=86](http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=6089488&postcount=86)
(at the bottom) Hopefully that will work..

@draugr
Make sure you copied the module..
cd into the linuxwacom folder then run:
sudo cp ./src/2.6.27/wacom.ko /lib/modules/`uname -r`/kernel/drivers/input/tablet/wacom.ko

then edit your xorg.conf and replace it with the one below...
Make sure to back it up!!!!
You should then be able to restart and everything should work.
Kory

edit: replaced xorg with one that will work... Thanks chadmerkert!)

I think that I should add it here:

```
Section "Device"
	Identifier  "aticonfig-Device[0]-0"
	Driver      "fglrx"

### Post by chadmerkert on 2008-11-08
gali98, The Xorg file you gave me doesn't allow X to start, and kept giving me:
 
Fatal server error:
no screens found
giving up.

But adding the two lines that Loïc2 mentioned:

Identifier    "Default Layout"
Screen        "Default Screen"

to the Section "ServerLayout" fixed that, and now ubuntu is running great with the touch screen fully functional! 

Thank you both, for helping me!

Attached is my working xorg.conf file, so people can see what I did, and hopefully help someone else. Im running an HP tx2500z CTO, 2.2GHz AMD Turion X2, with 4GB RAM, and ATI Radeon Graphics card.


I'm still working on getting the Rotation working, and will report back when I do.

### Post by chadmerkert on 2008-11-09
Hey makosgaming,

as long as you do sudo modprobe wacom after sudo rmmod wacom, that should be fine. As for your problem, i was haveing the same problem just yesterday, and what i did was continue on to editing xorg.conf anyway, and it worked for me. I have the same laptop, so my xorg.conf file should work great for you. I will attach it. What you should do is back up your current xorg.conf file by doing 


```
sudo cp /etc/X11/xorg.conf /etc/X11/xorg.conf.bak
```

which will copy your current xorg.conf to xorg.conf.bak, so if you need to restore it later.

then after you download my xorg.conf, say to your desktop, do the following, making sure to replace the InsertYourUserNameHere with your user name!!

```

sudo cp /home/InsertYourUserNameHere/Desktop/xorg.conf.txt /etc/X11/xorg.conf

```

which will copy the file you downloaded and replace your current xorg.conf file


then try rebooting and see if that helps at all! if you run in to any problems, you can restore your old xorg.conf by doing:

```

sudo cp /etc/X11/xorg.conf.bak /etc/X11/xorg.conf

```


Hope this helps, any other problems, let us know.

---

### Post by chadmerkert on 2008-11-09
a_toff,

I have had that same problem, the only way I can figure out to fix it is to boot up as normal, and log in. once logged in, the screen will probably just be blank with a mouse! what you can do is press ALT-F2 and even though you won't see anything type  

```
xrandr -o normal
```

which should fix your display, but only until you reboot, so to fix it permanently you need to disable xrandr, at lease until we find a way to fix it properly!

```
sudo aticonfig --set-pcs-str="DDX,EnableRandr12,FALSE"
```

Hope this helps

---

### Post by th89 on 2008-11-09
> **keabler said:**
> 
can some one tell me how to calibrate the touchscreen? its not bad but im going to be picky lol

Just open up the console and type in
```
wacomcpl
```
That should give you a list of the devices. Just click the device you want to calibrate and there will be a bunch of options to calibrate stylus, touch, and other stuff.

---

### Post by chadmerkert on 2008-11-10
regarding a_toff and my problem, it seems like the rotation works a lot better if you have Visual Effects set to none.

### Post by gali98 on 2008-11-12
@murphy 
since we are on Intrepid (though its mainly because of the 2.6.27 kernel) we no longer have to use those options.. On Hardy we did, but the power management and other things got better. That is how it is at least on the tx2000... I'm not sure on the tx2500...

@dharmabummed..
The only reason your wireless may have stopped working is because the kernel was updated.. First, go into the restricted Drivers (System->Administration->Hardware Drivers)
and disable then enable the Broadcom. Then restart and it should fix that. As far as the last problem.. as the poster above hints, you either did not download it, or you are not cd'd to your desktop.
Just use "cd Desktop" and if you downloaded it right you will be able to continue.

Keabler I suggest first running these two commands:
sudo apt-get install wacom-tools xserver-xorg-input-wacom
sudo apt-get purge wacom-tools xserver-xorg-input-wacom

then cd into the linuxwacom folder and run
sudo src/uninstall

that should remove everything. Then delete the linux wacom folder and start over again.
Try and use that xorg.conf again. If it still does not work, upload your present xorg.conf as that is usually the source of the problem.
Kory

### Post by zoomy942 on 2008-11-14
To rotate the screen, I use these 2 scripts.

open the text editor and paste this

```
#!/bin/sh
           xrandr -o left
           xsetwacom set "stylus" Rotate CCW
```

and save it as rotate.sh and palce it somewhere.  

then be sure to run 

sudo chmod +x ./rotate.sh

then make another text editor file with this

```
#!/bin/sh
           xrandr -o normal
           xsetwacom set "stylus" Rotate none
```

and save it as normal.sh then run that same sudo command above on it.

then, what i did was make shortcuts on my main menu for them, until i figure out how to map them to hardware keys.

---
