### Post by gali98 on 2008-11-14
Okay... Here we go again :)
Because there is so much to answer, I am splitting this into sections...

**WIRELESS AND VIDEO ISSUES**
On the wireless issues, all I can suggest is to make sure Hardware drivers are on (System->Administration->Hardware Drivers).
You may also try removing them, then installing again.

On the video issues, that almost has to be the video driver, which I'm not sure if there is any way to fix (beyond my scope anyway)


**Testing Pressure**

The best way I know is to use Gimp.. also you may have a look at tablet apps, which has a good visual tool for using pressure:
[http://www.alexmac.cc/tablet-apps/](http://www.alexmac.cc/tablet-apps/)

**Suspend**
The suspend issue seems to be a problem with the tx2500s.. I am going to look into the issue, but without a tx2500, I can't do a whole lot of testing. 
[B]
On the backup thing...[/B]
 you could just use Gparted to Copy the whole partition..
Copying all the files would work as well.
And Taring.. But I'm not any expert on the matter.

[B]
Okay to get rotating to map...[/B]
I only know how to do it on Metacity (i.e. without Compiz and visual graphics on.. If you are on Compiz, I am sure someone else can help you, or by looking through the options you can figure it out yourself)

First open a terminal and use the command xev
to find the keycodes of the buttons you want to use (Note: some of the keys on the laptop, namely the rotate button and the one beside it do not have Keycodes and therefore do not work.... I use the button under the DVD key  and it works fine.)

So after you find the keycode, 
run the command:
```
gedit ~/.Xmodmap
```
and in there 
make a line for each key like so:
```
keycode (keycode you got) = XF86Launch? 
```  
where is ? is a number 0 to 9. An example is:
```
keycode 201 = XF86Launch0
```
then save that and log out and log back in. You should get a dialog about Xmodmaps.. Basically you need to move the files so that it shows as being loaded. A way to check is to run xev again, and if it works you will see XF86Launch in the output..

So now press Alt+F2 and type gconf-editor and hit enter.
Go to ```
apps->metacity->global keybindings.
``` 
double click on run_command_1 and for the value put XF86Launch0 (or the name for whatever key you want) and click okay.
Now go to ```
apps->metacity->keybinding commands
```
and double click command_1. for the value use:
```
sh /path/to/your/script
```
As you can probably guess, the run_command and command match up (run_command_1 and command_1 match, run_command_2 and command_2, etc...)
Now only one more thing!
So that the keys will work right, you need to run the two following commands:
```
sudo update-rc.d -f hotkey-setup remove
sudo update-rc.d  hotkey-setup start 99 1 2 3 4 5 6 .
```
(You need that period!)

Now reboot to see if it works (and it should... :))

**Okay moving on: Mars Thrax**

Here is what I suggest:
Follow my tutorial for all but the xorg.conf  and install the new version of linux wacom which probably has more support than that tutorial for serial tablets..
Here are all the basic commands you will need. Just run them in order:

```
cd ~/Desktop

wget http://prdownloads.sourceforge.net/linuxwacom/linuxwacom-0.8.1-6.tar.bz2

sudo apt-get update

sudo apt-get install build-essential libx11-dev libxi-dev x11proto-input-dev xserver-xorg-dev tk8.4-dev tcl8.4-dev libncurses5-dev

sudo apt-get upgrade

sudo apt-get install wacom-tools xserver-xorg-input-wacom

sudo apt-get purge wacom-tools xserver-xorg-input-wacom

sudo apt-get install linux-headers-generic

tar xjvf linuxwacom-0.8.1-6.tar.bz2

cd linuxwacom-0.8.1-6

./configure --enable-wacom --prefix=/usr

make

sudo make install

sudo cp ./src/2.6.27/wacom.ko /lib/modules/`uname -r`/kernel/drivers/input/tablet/wacom.ko
```

If you don't want to run all of it then just download the script below I made and run it. Just put in your password when prompted.
Now restart (and it may take three or four reboots!) and it should work. If not, please upload your xorg.conf..
[B]
martinjochimsen[/B]

I suggest you also run the above commands, (or run the script)
and if you are still having the problems please upload your xorg.conf for me to look at..

Okay I think I covered everything.. (it was like writing a whole other tutorial :))
Post back guys!
Kory

---

Below is my xorg.conf:
```
# xorg.conf (X.Org X Window System server configuration file)
Section "Monitor"
	Identifier	"Configured Monitor"
EndSection

Section "Screen"
	Identifier	"Default Screen"
	Monitor		"Configured Monitor"
	Device		"Configured Video Device"
	SubSection "Display"
		Virtual	2432 864
	EndSubSection
EndSection

Section "InputDevice"
	Identifier      "stylus"
	Driver          "wacom"
	Option          "Device"        "/dev/ttyS0"
	Option          "Type"          "stylus"
	Option          "ForceDevice"   "ISDV4"
	Option          "Mode"          "absolute"
	Option          "SendCoreEvents"        "true"
EndSection

Section "InputDevice"
	Identifier      "eraser"
	Driver          "wacom"
	Option          "Device"        "/dev/ttyS0"
	Option          "Type"          "eraser"
	Option          "ForceDevice"   "ISDV4"
	Option          "Mode"          "absolute"
	Option          "SendCoreEvents"        "true"
EndSection

Section "InputDevice"
	Identifier      "cursor"
	Driver          "wacom"
	Option          "Device"        "/dev/ttyS0"
	Option          "Type"          "cursor"
	Option          "ForceDevice"   "ISDV4"
	Option          "Mode"          "absolute"
	Option          "SendCoreEvents"        "true"
EndSection

Section "ServerLayout"
	Identifier	"Default Layout"
	screen		"Default Screen"
	InputDevice     "stylus"        "SendCoreEvents"
	InputDevice     "eraser"        "SendCoreEvents"
	InputDevice     "cursor"        "SendCoreEvents"
EndSection

Section "Device"
	Identifier	"Configured Video Device"
EndSection

```

### Post by olejorgen on 2008-11-15
Mars:
```

Wacom xf86WcmWrite ISDV4_STOP error : Input/output error

```
I guess this is the problem, not sure exacly what it means though.

Try ```
xxd /dev/ttyS0
``` and move the stylus close to the screen. Do you get any output?

Also:
```

lshal | less
```
Search for ttyS0 or Wacom to find the section looking something like below.
(press '/' to search, 'n' to go to the next match)
```

udi = '/org/freedesktop/Hal/devices/pnp_WACf004_serial_platform_0'
  info.capabilities = {'serial'} (string list)
  info.category = 'serial'  (string)
  info.parent = '/org/freedesktop/Hal/devices/pnp_WACf004'  (string)
  info.product = 'Wacom Serial Tablet PC Pen Tablet/Digitizer'  (string)
  info.subsystem = 'tty'  (string)
  info.udi = '/org/freedesktop/Hal/devices/pnp_WACf004_serial_platform_0'  (string)
  linux.device_file = '/dev/ttyS0'  (string)
  linux.hotplug_type = 2  (0x2)  (int)
  linux.subsystem = 'tty'  (string)
  linux.sysfs_path = '/sys/class/tty/ttyS0'  (string)
  **serial.device = '/dev/ttyS0'  (string)**
  serial.originating_device = '/org/freedesktop/Hal/devices/pnp_WACf004'  (string)
  serial.port = 0  (0x0)  (int)
  serial.type = 'platform'  (string)

```
Verify that you have the bold line.

### Post by a_toff on 2008-11-15
> **gali98 said:**
> Okay I have a few things for you to try....

First edit /boot/grub/menu.lst

and find the line that looks like:
# defoptions=quiet splash
and make it
# defoptions=quiet splash i8042.reset

then run
sudo update-grub
and restart and try suspending...

### Post by Mars Thrax on 2008-11-15
For people working on screen rotation and getting key bindings to work (even with Compiz):

Check out the sections on rotating the screen and getting the bezel buttons to work [here]("https://wiki.ubuntu.com/LaptopTestingTeam/ToshibaPortegeM700"). It has generic instructions using xbindkeys to create key bindings pretty easily. I'm using them with Compiz enabled on my M700 without issue. Just make sure you add an entry for starting xbindkeys to your sessions to make sure it is started on login.

2) My screen rotates, but the input doesn't. I am using an individual script for each direction. Below is an example of the rotate-left script (the rest are the same, but with appropriate changes in the rotation direction and input rotation commands:

```

#!/bin/bash
xrandr -o left
xsetwacom set "stylus" Rotate CCW
xsetwacom set "cursor" Rotate CCW
xsetwacom set "eraser" Rotate CCW

```

So, the xrander -o <direction> works fine, but none of the xsetwacom instructions work at all. Typed at the command line, those commands produce no output, but also do not rotate the input.

Any ideas on these new problems?

### Post by Ibycus on 2008-11-15
Hi guys,

First let me say thanks to all the contributors of the forums.  I just jumped in with Ubuntu and you guys are definitely a key to its success.

That being said, I've been trying to get my Fujitsu T4210 tablet up and running, and have been surfing the forums trying various remedies with little success.  My level of linux know-how is pretty low, so forgive any completely nonsensical comments.  Here's where I stand.
```

wacdump -f tcp /dev/ttyS0 

```
shows activity


```
sudo xxd /dev/ttyS0
```
used to show activity, but something I've done seems to have mucked that up.

Things I've tried:
editing the xorg.conf (more than once)
installing the linuxwacom driver (more than once)
editing rc.local to include the following script:
```
setserial /dev/ttys0 port 0x0220 irq 4 autoconfigure
```

Seems to me theres still some problem getting the device to latch into the cursor.  I've tried waving my stylus all over my screen with no success, so I doubt it's a calibration issue... but who knows (:

As requested in one of the earlier posts, here's my install information, along with the (I believe more pertinent) xorg.conf information.

I am running the Ibex version of Ubuntu, apt-updated and whatnot.

/etc/X11/xorg.conf:
```


Section "Device"
	Identifier	"Configured Video Device"
EndSection

Section "Monitor"
	Identifier	"Configured Monitor"
EndSection

Section "Screen"
	Identifier	"Default Screen"
	Monitor		"Configured Monitor"
	Device		"Configured Video Device"
EndSection

Section "InputDevice"
  Driver        "wacom"
  Identifier    "stylus"
  Option        "Device"        "/dev/ttyS0"          # SERIAL ONLY
  Option        "Type"          "stylus"
  Option        "ForceDevice"   "ISDV4"               # Serial Tablet PC ONLY
EndSection


Section "InputDevice"
  Driver        "wacom"
  Identifier    "eraser"
  Option        "Device"        "/dev/ttyS0"          # SERIAL ONLY
  Option        "Type"          "eraser"
  Option        "ForceDevice"   "ISDV4"               # Serial Tablet PC ONLY
EndSection


Section "InputDevice"
  Driver        "wacom"
  Identifier    "cursor"
  Option        "Device"        "/dev/ttyS0"          # SERIAL ONLY
  Option        "Type"          "cursor"
  Option        "ForceDevice"   "ISDV4"               # Serial Tablet PC ONLY
EndSection


```

The configure output (and input) are attached.

The make output (and input) are attached.

The make install output (and input) are attached.

### Post by Ibycus on 2008-11-15
Okay, so I've made marginal progress: I now know another symptom (but not the cause) of my problems.  fresh from reboot, xxd will not respond to stylus input.  However, wacdump will (though it stutters at first), and subsequently, xxd will respond again.  

This leads me to believe that wacdump is initializing something (I have no idea what).

Also, even after this "initialization glitch", I do not have stylus cursor control, so there's still likely a problem one step up.

Thanks for your help.

---

### Post by Ibycus on 2008-11-15
After some more fumbling, I realized the problem was with my server loadout section, which i had deleted after repeated issues with it.  There were two sources of the issues, which when solved left me with a working stylus:

1 - if you have any devices in your "server loadout" that weren't previously defined in the file, they will cause errors, and 

2 - for some reason copying and pasting the server loadout data had left me with an EndSection that wasn't actually on its own line, but instead was just spaced far enough to appear so.  

I hope this helps anyone with similar problems

-Ibycus

---

Update:

It turns out that I had a (possibly old?) version of xsetwacom in /usr/local/bin, and just running "xsetwacom ..." would default to that (instead of the correct one in /usr/bin). Using the full path in my scripts seems to have fixed the problem.

I am still having trouble with my touchscreen not being calibrated (wacomcpl returns the useless GUI described before), but that is my only real issue at this point.

Aside from the touch screen though, I do have one other thing I'd like to get working. At home, I hook my tablet up to my monitor so I can dual screen. Everything works fine, except that my pen does not confine itself only to the tablet screen (the calibration for it seems to be correct...moving the pen to the top left of the tablet screen puts the cursor at the top left position between the two displays, and vice versa). Any ideas on how to make sure that pen/touch input only renders the cursor on the tablet screen?

### Post by a_toff on 2008-11-16
Hey folks,
Just got screen-rotation working by following th89's [guide]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=6107863&postcount=238"), and using the script he wrote... Thanks for the info th89! I'm running Intrepid, so I can confirm that the following line,

```
#This line is for use with 8.04 (Hardy Heron):
rotation="$(xrandr -q --verbose | sed -n '2 {p;q}' | cut -d' ' -f5)"
```

works for Intrepid too!

Just a quick question though... when I use right-click/Properties on my ".rotate" file to try to make it executable, I still get a dialog window popping up when I try to run the file... how do I force it to be automatically run as an executable?

thanks again! next problem I'll be tackling is screen button mapping... I'll chime in soon to let you know how it goes.

### Post by th89 on 2008-11-17
> **a_toff said:**
> 
Just a quick question though... when I use right-click/Properties on my ".rotate" file to try to make it executable, I still get a dialog window popping up when I try to run the file... how do I force it to be automatically run as an executable?

This is pretty easy actually, all you have to do is create a shortcut to the file, and make sure the file is marked as executable.

```

### Post by th89 on 2008-11-17
> **a_toff said:**
> @th89:
Oh well, rotation works well now, so I'm happy. Just wondering though, how do I set the rotation script to run automatically when double-clicked? I have it set as executable but I always get a dialog window which asks whether I want to run it in terminal, display it, or run normally...


Yeah, all you have to do is create a launcher (shortcut is windows terminology, my bad). Right click on the desktop and select create launcher. Type is application, Name is whatever you want, Command would be:
```
/home/username/.rotate (or .rotate.sh, depending on what you named it)
```
When you run that, it wont prompt anymore, but will just rotate the screen.

> **a_toff said:**
> ps... have you played around with the IR remote at all yet?

HOWEVER, I used the remote with Boxee (based on XMBC - its in alpha and invite only at the moment - see [THIS POST]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=979953") to get an invite) and it performed incredibly. Almost all the buttons worked, and like they should've. I was actually astounded. The experience was not unlike Windows Media Center.

Hope this helps.

### Post by a_toff on 2008-11-18
> **th89 said:**
> For those wanting to use Xournal in Intrepid. Apparently there is a bug with libgnome canvas, that causes Xournal to be unusable. 

To install this patch, just download these debs into the same folder, cd into that folder, and run:
```
sudo dpkg -i libgnomecanvas*.deb
```

...

This fixed the problem I had with Xournal not working correctly. Before Xournal would be very laggy, would not draw correctly when the window was resized, and other problems. After this patch everything seems to be working correctly as far as I can tell.

### Post by th89 on 2008-11-19
Glad that patch worked! Xournal is the most useful tablet app I've come across. You may want to check out "CellWriter" and "EasyStroke" (both are available via Synaptic or "apt-get install"). CellWriter will give you an on-screen keyboard with handwriting recognition. The handwriting takes quite a bit of training, but it seems to be a decent application. EasyStroke is a gestures program that is loaded with features. I'd recommend checking both of them out.

Also, since you are are running ubuntu 64 bit, you may want to check out the [x86_64 thread]("http://ubuntuforums.org/forumdisplay.php?f=134"), and [this post]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=368607") as well. They cover a lot of common questions and stuff that may help you.

### Post by a_toff on 2008-11-22
@ Docaltmed:  if you skim through this thread you'll find that many of us have had the same trouble... the tutorial gives the impression that you will have stylus recognition BEFORE editing your xorg.conf file. This is NOT the case, however. Your xorg.conf file needs to be set-up before you'll have pen recognition. See [this]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=6128555&postcount=250") post by gali98, on [page 25]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=870640&page=25") of this thread.

Try using the xorg.conf file that gali98 provided for me there (remembering of course to back up your xorg.conf file first!).

--------------------

@ everyone else:

Have you seen this [Tips & Tricks page]("http://easystroke.wiki.sourceforge.net/TipsAndTricks") on the EasyStroke wiki? It talks about setting up a daemon to automatially adjust the Wacom settings with screen-rotation:

[QUOTE=EasyStroke Wiki]Don't use Rotate Scripts
There are tons of applications out there that allow you to change screen resolution and rotation. However, as a tablet user you will also need tell the wacom driver to rotate pen input. So people ditch these applications and replace them by something much worse: Custom-made rotate scripts that must be used if you want to your pen to be usable after rotate - very annoying and cumbersome to set up.
But Xrandr is perfectly capable of notifying applications of screen changes, so a much better solution is to have a tiny daemon that performs the necessary actions whenever the screen is rotated. The file  rotate.c is a simple example of this: It will both rotate the pen and, if you're running gnome, adjust the orientation of subpixel smoothing, which will make fonts less blurry.[/QUOTE]

Does anyone have any thoughts on this?

---

### Post by martinjochimsen on 2008-11-22
Hi Docaltmed

Take a look at my xorg. I'v got a 2590oe and my xorg looked exactly like yours to begin with. After installing the wacom-thing (I followed gali98s guide last edited November the 3th) I pasted some parts of my old xorg from when I used 8.04.
You could try how mine xorg works on your computer.

Martin




# xorg.conf (X.Org X Window System server configuration file)
#
# This file was generated by dexconf, the Debian X Configuration tool, using
# values from the debconf database.
#
# Edit this file with caution, and see the xorg.conf manual page.
# (Type "man xorg.conf" at the shell prompt.)
#
# This file is automatically updated on xserver-xorg package upgrades *only*
# if it has not been modified since the last upgrade of the xserver-xorg
# package.
#
# Note that some configuration settings that could be done previously
# in this file, now are automatically configured by the server and settings
# here are ignored.
#
# If you have edited this file but would like it to be automatically updated
# again, run the following command:
#   sudo dpkg-reconfigure -phigh xserver-xorg

Section "Monitor"
	Identifier	"Configured Monitor"
EndSection

Section "InputDevice"
	Identifier	"Generic Keyboard"
	Driver		"kbd"
	Option		"XkbRules"	"xorg"
	Option		"XkbModel"	"pc105"
	Option		"XkbLayout"	"dk"
EndSection

Section "InputDevice"
	Identifier	"Configured Mouse"
	Driver		"mouse"
	Option		"CorePointer"
EndSection

Section "InputDevice"
	Identifier	"Synaptics Pad"
	Driver		"synaptics"
	Option		"SendCoreEvents"	"true"
	Option		"Device"	"/dev/psaux"
	Option		"Protocol"	"auto-dev"
	Option		"HorizEdgeScroll"	"0"
EndSection

Section "InputDevice"
Identifier "stylus"
Driver "wacom"
Option "Type" "stylus"
Option "USB" "on"
Option "Device" "/dev/input/by-path/pci-0000:00:14.5-usb-0:2:1.0-event-mouse"
Option "Button2" "3" # make side-switch a right button
Option "TopX" "225"
Option "TopY" "225"
Option "BottomX" "26300"
Option "BottomY" "16375"
EndSection

Section "InputDevice"
Identifier "touch"
Driver "wacom"
Option "Type" "touch"
Option "USB" "on"
Option "Device" "/dev/input/by-path/pci-0000:00:14.5-usb-0:2:1.1-event-"
Option "TopX" "200"
Option "TopY" "225"
Option "BottomX" "4000"
Option "BottomY" "3875"
EndSection

Section "InputDevice"
Identifier "eraser"
Driver "wacom"
Option "Type" "eraser"
Option "Device" "/dev/input/by-path/pci-0000:00:14.5-usb-0:2:1.0-event-mouse"
Option "USB" "on"
EndSection

Section "Screen"
	Identifier	"Default Screen"
	Monitor		"Configured Monitor"
	Device		"Configured Video Device"
	DefaultDepth	24
EndSection

Section "ServerLayout"
	Identifier	"Default Layout"
  	screen 		"Default Screen"
	Inputdevice	"Synaptics Pad"
	Inputdevice "stylus"	"SendCoreEvents"
	Inputdevice "touch"	"SendCoreEvents"
	Inputdevice "eraser"	"SendCoreEvents"
EndSection

Section "Module"
	Load	"glx"
EndSection

Section "Device"
	Identifier	"Configured Video Device"
	Driver	"fglrx"
EndSection

### Post by th89 on 2008-11-22
> **a_toff said:**
> 
@ everyone else:

Have you seen this [Tips & Tricks page]("http://easystroke.wiki.sourceforge.net/TipsAndTricks") on the EasyStroke wiki? It talks about setting up a daemon to automatially adjust the Wacom settings with screen-rotation:
>                      Originally Posted by **EasyStroke Wiki**                                      
                 [I]Don't use Rotate Scripts
There are tons of applications out there that allow you to change screen resolution and rotation. However, as a tablet user you will also need tell the wacom driver to rotate pen input. So people ditch these applications and replace them by something much worse: Custom-made rotate scripts that must be used if you want to your pen to be usable after rotate - very annoying and cumbersome to set up.
But Xrandr is perfectly capable of notifying applications of screen changes, so a much better solution is to have a tiny daemon that performs the necessary actions whenever the screen is rotated. The file rotate.c is a simple example of this: It will both rotate the pen and, if you're running gnome, adjust the orientation of subpixel smoothing, which will make fonts less blurry.[/I]
Does anyone have any thoughts on this?

Yeah, I have two thoughts. One, the rotate script works perfectly, so why swap it out for something that provides no clear advantages? The second thing is, why would you swap out a runtime script for a constantly running background application? If your like me, you don't really rotate that much, so having a constantly running application to provide the same features a simple script could do, seems worthless.

There may be other advantages I'm not aware of, but the script provides all the functionality I need, or want.

### Post by Tom Jaeger on 2008-11-23
> **th89 said:**
> Yeah, I have two thoughts. One, the rotate script works perfectly, so why swap it out for something that provides no clear advantages? The second thing is, why would you swap out a runtime script for a constantly running background application? If your like me, you don't really rotate that much, so having a constantly running application to provide the same features a simple script could do, seems worthless.
Maybe rotate scripts don't have any advantage for you because you already spent the time setting them up and you're okay with having to use one particular method for rotating the screen, but that's certainly not true for everyone.  Rotate scripts are a user interface nightmare:  The same task (rotating the display) has to be done in two completely different ways depending on whether you are on a Tablet PC or not.  On a regular system, there many different ways of rotating the screen and they are easily accessible to a non-technical user (System -> Preferences -> Screen Resolution, several randr applets, xrandr, etc.), yet on a Tablet PC the user is forced to use an obscure rotate script.  That doesn't seem right to me.

> **Favux said:**
> I haven't tried it because looking at it I only see the stylus mentioned, not the eraser or cursor.  Both of those are handled in my xsetwacom script.  Besides I'm not sure how to implement it, Sessions?
This is not how the wacom driver works.  If you rotate one of the devices, you rotate them all, so yes, my daemon does rotate the eraser.  Btw, if you're on a Tablet PC, you might as well remove the cursor device from your xorg.conf, it doesn't do anything.

I've packaged the wacomrotate daemon to simplify setting up proper wacom rotation: Just install one of [these]("http://ppa.launchpad.net/thjaeger/ubuntu/pool/main/w/wacomrotate/") packages, restart the X server and you'll be able to use the "Screen Resolution" dialog, gnome-randr-applet or whatever tool you prefer to rotate your screen.

If we could figure out a way to reliable detect whether we're on a Tablet PC (right now the daemon checks if the tablet is connected via a serial port, but I've disabled in the autostart entry), it would probably be a good idea to include it in the wacom-tools package.

---

If we could figure out a way to reliable detect whether we're on a Tablet PC (right now the daemon checks if the tablet is connected via a serial port, but I've disabled in the autostart entry), it would probably be a good idea to include it in the wacom-tools package.

### Post by martinjochimsen on 2008-11-23
To Docaltmed post 357:

In this thread [http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=870640&page=32](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=870640&page=32) (post 312) I wrote about the same problem with wacom not working after reboot. Gali answered right after that I should try the guide once again:



cd ~/Desktop

wget [http://prdownloads.sourceforge.net/linuxwacom/linuxwacom-0.8.1-6.tar.bz2](http://prdownloads.sourceforge.net/linuxwacom/linuxwacom-0.8.1-6.tar.bz2)

sudo apt-get update

sudo apt-get install build-essential libx11-dev libxi-dev x11proto-input-dev xserver-xorg-dev tk8.4-dev tcl8.4-dev libncurses5-dev

sudo apt-get upgrade

sudo apt-get install wacom-tools xserver-xorg-input-wacom

sudo apt-get purge wacom-tools xserver-xorg-input-wacom

sudo apt-get install linux-headers-generic

tar xjvf linuxwacom-0.8.1-6.tar.bz2

cd linuxwacom-0.8.1-6

./configure --enable-wacom --prefix=/usr

make

sudo make install

sudo cp ./src/2.6.27/wacom.ko /lib/modules/`uname -r`/kernel/drivers/input/tablet/wacom.ko



...and suddenly it worked after every reboot!
Also make sure that there only is one "action" for wacom in system->preferences->sessions (as gali also suggests)
Click on add and for the command write "~/.xinitrc.
I hope this will help?!?

Martin :-)

---

### Post by Tom Jaeger on 2008-11-23
> **Favux said:**
> It is worse than that, my table pc connects to the built in tablet via USB.  I agree and would like to see your rotation daemon included in the tools package as the more tablet support the better.
Being a newbie I still don't understand how to implement your daemon.  Great so I've downloaded it and I downloaded Grandr (thanks for pointing out it's existence by the way).
Sorry, I actually meant gnome-randr-applet, which will appear as "Display Geometry Switcher" in the "Add to panel" dialog. But you don't actually have to install anything:  'System -> Preferences -> Screen Resolution -> Show Displays in Panel' will place in icon in your tray.

> So now I have another GUI other than the nVidia rotation gui.
If the nvidia driver properly implements the xrandr extension, then you should be able to use their gui as well.

> Grandr (called Mutiple Screens in System>Administration) by the way doesn't rotate left or right, it says "User set screen size larger than max screen size."
It's possible that you need to do some extra work to get randr working on nvidia hardware.  I found this thread, I'm not sure it still applies:
[http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=682821](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=682821)

> 
Anyway say I fumble my way into figuring out Grandr and have your daemon active (again do I put it in Sessions so it runs on boot?  What directory do you want your C code in?  Is there a readme.txt in the install package?).

If you install the package, the daemon will automatically start the next time you restart X.  There's nothing else you need to do.

> 
Now do I need a macro to call up Grandr tab over to rotation and then pick rotate left or whatever?

The proper way to rotate the display from the command line is
```
xrandr -o <normal,inverted,left,right,0,1,2,3>
```

### Post by th89 on 2008-11-23
> **Tom Jaeger said:**
>  ...yet on a Tablet PC the user is forced to use an obscure rotate script.  That doesn't seem right to me. 

Actually, its not all that odd. All you have to do is rotate the screen, then rotate your input device (in this case, your tablet input). By using a daemon you are simply waiting until your application sees that screen was rotated, then rotates the input, by using the same commands. A daemon will not do anything different then a rotate script. If you have specialized needs, a script is also easier to configure. I wrote my first rotate script after only using linux for 2 weeks, so they're not THAT difficult.

---

### Post by Favux on 2008-11-24
Thanks for getting back so quickly Tom.
You're right, for my particular tablet the nVidia section of my Xorg.conf needs to be modified as follows:
```
Section "Device"
	Identifier	"Configured Video Device"
	Driver		"nvidia"
	Option		"NoLogo"	"True"
Option "RandRRotation"  "on"
EndSection
```
Notice I did not indent the line I added, so I'd know it was the one I added.

I now realize that I had a brain fart when I wrote cursor before, I meant touch (or in my idiosyncratic lingo my touch-cursor).  I apologize.  You had no way of knowing my tablet pc also included a touch screen.  The xorg.conf also needs the following for stylus:
```
# commented out by update-manager, HAL is now used
Section "InputDevice"
Identifier "stylus"
Driver "wacom"
Option "Type" "stylus"
Option "USB" "on"
Option "Device" "/dev/input/by-path/pci-0000:00:0b.1-usb-0:2.3:1.0-event-mouse"
Option "Button2" "3" # make side-switch a right button
Option "TopX" "225"
Option "TopY" "225"
Option "BottomX" "26300"
Option "BottomY" "16375"
EndSection
```
Similar sections have to be added for eraser and touch.  In addition in the ServerLayout section I had to add:
```
Section "ServerLayout"
	Identifier	"Default Layout"
  screen "Default Screen"
# commented out by update-manager, HAL is now used
#	Inputdevice	"Synaptics Pad"
# commented out by update-manager, HAL is now used
Inputdevice "stylus"	"SendCoreEvents"
# commented out by update-manager, HAL is now used
Inputdevice "touch"	"SendCoreEvents"
# commented out by update-manager, HAL is now used
Inputdevice "eraser"	"SendCoreEvents"
EndSection
```
Also had to change Synaptic TouchPad to Synaptic Pad so it wouldn't interfere with "touch".  Notice from the header of the first section and all through the rest that Intrepid kindly remarked all these out rendering the tablet inoperative.  Function was suppose to be supplied out of the box by HAL, but it wasn't.  Even if it had been there is a catch:  the only thing functioning would have been the stylus.  According to some bug reports on launchpad there is a limitation on HAL communicating through dBus that limits you to one input device per tablet (whether serial or usb) and no workaround has yet been developed.

Now to get to the main point.  I think I now follow you.  You are saying that a tablet pc user should be able to rotate his screen, by what ever means he chooses, and the other things like the stylus should automatically rotate also.  This is what your daemon accomplishes.  It doesn't "magically" detect the physical rotation of the screen and change orientation like Vista does on my tablet.  After xrandr flips the screen, by whatever method chosen, it flips the orientation of stylus, eraser, and touch to automatically match that orientation.  Your daemon makes that aspect of screen rotation transparent.  I hope I'm right and have finally understood you.

But still, since Intrepid doesn't detect the physical rotation of the screen, something still has to call xrandr to flip the orientation whether its the nVidia gui (which works), or the Grandr gui (which at least inverts), or the terminal command "xrandr -o <normal,inverted,left,right,0,1,2,3>" or the famous bash shell script executed in terminal:
```
#Uncomment next line to use script on 6.06 (Dapper Drake) (and comment later one):
#rotation="$(xrandr -q | grep 'Current rotation' | cut -d' ' -f4)"

#This line is for use with 8.04 (Hardy Heron):
rotation="$(xrandr -q --verbose | sed -n '2 {p;q}' | cut -d' ' -f5)"

case "$rotation" in
    normal)
        xrandr -o right
        xsetwacom set "stylus" Rotate CW
	xsetwacom set "touch" Rotate CW
	xsetwacom set "eraser" Rotate CW
        ;;
    right)
        xrandr -o inverted
        xsetwacom set "stylus" Rotate HALF
	xsetwacom set "touch" Rotate HALF
	xsetwacom set "eraser" Rotate HALF
        ;;
    inverted)
        xrandr -o left
        xsetwacom set "stylus" Rotate CCW
	xsetwacom set "touch" Rotate CCW
	xsetwacom set "eraser" Rotate CCW
        ;;
    left)
        xrandr -o normal
        xsetwacom set "stylus" Rotate NONE
	xsetwacom set "touch" Rotate NONE
	xsetwacom set "eraser" Rotate NONE
        ;;
esac
```
Which I got from mirosol, or gali98, or maybe th89?

Now as I mentioned Intrepid broke the remaining 2 out of 4 tablet buttons I had (xev returns no keycode on any, whereas Hardy returned code on 2/4-sufficient to keybind to a cpl. useful functions including rotation).  But I don't want to go back to Hardy's kernel because I don't have to do the no irq, no aspci etc. (which maybe why the keycode is busted, but I'm not going to experiment).  The new kernel also seems to run cooler, i.e. with better multiple core support.  Of course it also broke wireless ...

Enough digression, in a practical sense how does your daemon help me?  It appears that at a minimum I have to set up an icon to invoke terminal to run a terminal command like "xrandr -o <normal,inverted,left,right,0,1,2,3>" or a gui like the gnome-randr-applet (which I located in Synaptic-thank you).  This seems mechanically to be equivalent to running the above script from an icon on my Cairo-dock.  This is so with or without keybinding to a tablet key.

Admittedly the script isn't ideal since it forces me to rotate through all 360 degrees but rotate left would require a second icon or key (if I had a working one).

I'm not trying to be argumentative.  I recognize as a newb I might well be too dense to understand what you're getting at.  From my point of view your rotation daemon plus the ability to detect the screen physically pivoting around and automatically triggering xrandr to change the orientation would be the ideal.

Thanks

Boom, back to standard orientation in two steps and without the 2 extra pauses while the screen reorients and resizes!  Since both daemon and script seem to coexist fine on the few app.s I tested with stylus and eraser and touch working fine why not keep both?  Since a rotation-left-scrip would require a second icon in the dock anyway it saves me from having to mess around to get a working script for the left rotation icon.

### Post by Tom Jaeger on 2008-11-24
> **Favux said:**
> Now to get to the main point.  I think I now follow you.  You are saying that a tablet pc user should be able to rotate his screen, by what ever means he chooses, and the other things like the stylus should automatically rotate also.  This is what your daemon accomplishes.
Exactly.

> 
But still, since Intrepid doesn't detect the physical rotation of the screen, something still has to call xrandr to flip the orientation whether its the nVidia gui (which works), or the Grandr gui (which at least inverts), or the terminal command "xrandr -o <normal,inverted,left,right,0,1,2,3>" or the famous bash shell script executed in terminal:
This doesn't even work on my system, but if it did, it would switch through all the possible rotations which I doubt anybody would want.  Here's how I would accomplish switching between regular and left orientation (this needs the wacomrotate daemon, of course)
```
xrandr -q | grep -q '+\w* (' && xrandr -o left || xrandr -o normal
```

> 
Enough digression, in a practical sense how does your daemon help me?  It appears that at a minimum I have to set up an icon to invoke terminal to run a terminal command like "xrandr -o <normal,inverted,left,right,0,1,2,3>" or a gui like the gnome-randr-applet (which I located in Synaptic-thank you).  This seems mechanically to be equivalent to running the above script from an icon on my Cairo-dock.  This is so with or without keybinding to a tablet key.

If this is the only way you're ever going to rotate your screen, then it probably won't make much of a difference (except for slightly simplifying the task of writing a rotate script).  It is beneficial in a more abstract sense, though.  The ultimate goal (though we're obviously quite far away from that) is to have things work out-of-the-box.  This of course entails that any way of rotating the screen will also rotate pen input, but it also means that it should be possible to set up a keyboard shortcut for rotating the screen in the gnome preferences.  Nobody is going to implement that (or accept a patch) if they need to fuss with xsetwacom to ensure that pen input is rotated properly.

> From my point of view your rotation daemon plus the ability to detect the screen physically pivoting around and automatically triggering xrandr to change the orientation would be the ideal.
Check the output of acpi_listen when you rotate the display.  It might generate an acpi event (my thinkpad does), in which case it shouldn't be too difficult to set up a script to automatically rotate the screen.

---

### Post by Favux on 2008-11-24
Oops!  I gloated to soon and have been punished for my hubris.

Tom,
No event recorded with acpi_listen.  Now I know there is an event, because Vista reacts to it.  Probably HP proprietary.  Interestingly enough I checked xev and got a keycode returned!  201 on my tablet "Q" key.  Ubuntu taketh away and Ubuntu returneth.

With your daemon active I lost orientation and calibration on eraser and touch somewhere between the second and fourth reboot.  I wasn't checking it every time.  I started checking when I noticed the stylus getting funky (not nearly as bad as eraser or touch though).  I tried to recalibrate by calling up wacomcpl in a terminal.  Wacomcpl sort of worked with the stylus (but not really), and not at all with the eraser or touch.  That appears to be a problem with your daemon, at least on my system, it interferes with wacomcpl and wacomcpl does not retain it's settings with reboot.  I tested this by removing wacomrotate from Sessions and rebooting.  I was then able to calibrate the stylus and touch with wacomcpl and it has retained the settings through multiple reboots.

Now maybe I should test wacomrotate on a "clean" system, one that I haven't used the xsetwacom script on, in other words.  Is it possible that the use of the xsetwacom script could mess up your wacom daemon and corrupt wacom tools i.e. wacomcpl?

I am on a HP TX2110us using AMD 64.

> This doesn't even work on my system, but if it did, it would switch through all the possible rotations which I doubt anybody would want.
You are right and you motivated me to finally look at the script.  Because the hinge on my HP TX2000 only allows rotation in one direction the following script turns out to do exactly what I need:
```
#This line is for use with 8.10 (Intrepid Ibex): 
rotation="$(xrandr -q --verbose | sed -n '2 {p;q}' | cut -d' ' -f5)" 

case "$rotation" in 
    normal) 
        xrandr -o right 
        xsetwacom set "stylus" Rotate CW 
        xsetwacom set "touch" Rotate CW 
        xsetwacom set "eraser" Rotate CW 
        ;; 
    right) 
        xrandr -o normal 
        xsetwacom set "stylus" Rotate NONE 
        xsetwacom set "touch" Rotate NONE 
        xsetwacom set "eraser" Rotate NONE 
        ;; 
esac

```
I'm embarrassed that it took me this long to address what turned out to be a simple fix.  Now with the script linked to a launcher on my dock I have exactly what I need in terms of script function.

I may go ahead and bind it to the "Q" key getting me back the tablet key functionality I had in Hardy.  I'm a little leary of the suddenly functioning keycode and I noticed in the pre-release sources we're due for another kernel upgrade.  Based on past experience this may break everything again.

I would be happy to work with you to see if you can get wacomrotate daemon to work on my system if you'd like to.

### Post by Favux on 2008-11-25
All right.  Further investigation showed that I had come down with a case of ". /etc/X11/Xsession" appearing in the xinitrc file.  Once I had commented it out Tom Jaeger's rotation daemon worked fine for stylus and eraser.  Although I didn't calibrate the stylus through wacomcpl, wacomcpl seems to now be working fine.  The wacomrotate daemon seems to co-exist fine with the xsetwacom script.

However touch does not work with the wacomrotate daemon, at least not yet.  The cursor is offset from my finger by about 2 inches.  This seems to be a constant offset.  I am reluctant to try and recalibrate touch through wacomcpl because touch is working fine through the above xsetwacom script.  So it will remain a mystery for now.

I was able to set Tom's command into a script with a launcher pointing to it and, except for touch, now have the wacomrotate daemon and the command providing the same rotation capability that the xsetwacom script delivers.

By the way since the TX2000 series pivots on a hinge clockwise 180 degrees (then locking down in tablet mode) and re-pivots the 180 degrees counter clockwise to get back to laptop mode.  It is a one way hinge and doesn't allow the 360 degree freedom of rotation that some of the other tablet pc's have.  So Tom's command:
```
xrandr -q | grep -q '+\w* (' && xrandr -o left || xrandr -o normal
```
should be (for right handers):
```
xrandr -q | grep -q '+\w* (' && xrandr -o right || xrandr -o normal
```

So there are options, especially if you don't need touch (at least for now).  Decisions, decisions.

---

### Post by Tom Jaeger on 2008-11-26
> **Favux said:**
> 
With your daemon active I lost orientation and calibration on eraser and touch somewhere between the second and fourth reboot.  I wasn't checking it every time.  I started checking when I noticed the stylus getting funky (not nearly as bad as eraser or touch though).  I tried to recalibrate by calling up wacomcpl in a terminal.  Wacomcpl sort of worked with the stylus (but not really), and not at all with the eraser or touch.  That appears to be a problem with your daemon, at least on my system, it interferes with wacomcpl and wacomcpl does not retain it's settings with reboot. This doesn't sound like a wacomrotate problem at all.  All wacomrotate does is call xsetwacom whenever the screen is rotated.  It's pretty obvious that the wacom driver for your tablet isn't as mature as the one for serial tablets.

> 
Now maybe I should test wacomrotate on a "clean" system, one that I haven't used the xsetwacom script on, in other words.  Is it possible that the use of the xsetwacom script could mess up your wacom daemon and corrupt wacom tools i.e. wacomcpl?

### Post by Tom Jaeger on 2008-11-26
> **Favux said:**
> However touch does not work with the wacomrotate daemon, at least not yet.  The cursor is offset from my finger by about 2 inches.  This seems to be a constant offset.  I am reluctant to try and recalibrate touch through wacomcpl because touch is working fine through the above xsetwacom script.  So it will remain a mystery for now.

But touch input *is* rotated?  You should probably check back with upstream how they intend your tablet to be rotated.  I know that for serial tablets, just one xsetwacom command is enough.  For now, I've added a -t option to wacomrotate ([packages in my ppa]("http://ppa.launchpad.net/thjaeger/ubuntu/pool/main/w/wacomrotate/")) to accommodate your situation.

### Post by Tom Jaeger on 2008-11-26
> **Favux said:**
> I tried your new deb package and with it *touch is not rotated*.  It's offset still and when I draw a line with my finger it moves 90 degrees to the line I am drawing.  I'm sorry but I don't know what you meant by a -t option.

Just start wacomrotate as "wacomrotate -f -t" instead of "wacomrotate -f".

> 
I finally discovered the output from the swivel hinge.  In /var/log/messages it says: [...]

These are the event devices that the wacom driver creates for the hinge.  You should be able to use xev to figure out what keycode they generate and then bind them to the appropriate xrandr command.

### Post by Favux on 2008-11-27
Update:

Success!  I tried to key bind Toms's command to the Q key and ran into problems.  Apparently HAL breaks key bindings.  Xev shows the key code and the fact that .Xmodmap is binding but Compiz command launch doesn't happen.  So I went to xorg.conf and removed the comments that Intrepid had installed in front of the keyboard section.  Reboot.  Presto key bindings back.

So using Tom's wacomrotation daemon and command has reactivated my Q key and given me the functioning tablet rotation that I had with Hardy.  Albeit more elegantly.

```
~$ sudo rmmod wacom
ERROR: Module wacom does not exist in /proc/modules
~$ sudo depmod -e
~$ sudo modprobe wacom

~$ dmesg | grep Wacom
[  296.882638] input: Wacom ISDv4 93 as /devices/pci0000:00/0000:00:14.5/usb7/7-2/7-2:1.0/input/input13
[  296.937393] input: Wacom ISDv4 93 as /devices/pci0000:00/0000:00:14.5/usb7/7-2/7-2:1.1/input/input14
[  297.043251] wacom: v1.49:USB Wacom Graphire and Wacom Intuos tablet driver

~$ dmesg | grep wacom
[  297.040335] usbcore: registered new interface driver wacom
[  297.043251] wacom: v1.49:USB Wacom Graphire and Wacom Intuos tablet driver

~$ ls -l /dev/inutput/by-path
total 0
lrwxrwxrwx 1 root root  9 2008-11-30 15:50 pci-0000:00:12.0-usb-0:1:1.0-event-mouse -> ../event2
lrwxrwxrwx 1 root root  9 2008-11-30 15:50 pci-0000:00:12.0-usb-0:1:1.0-mouse -> ../mouse1

lrwxrwxrwx 1 root root 10 2008-11-30 15:55 pci-0000:00:14.5-usb-0:2:1.0-event-mouse -> ../event13

~$ wacomcpl
wacomcpl: using TCLLIBPATH="[list  /usr/lib ]"

```

xorg.conf
```
Section "Monitor"
	Identifier	"Configured Monitor"
EndSection

Section "Screen"
	Identifier	"Default Screen"
	Monitor		"Configured Monitor"
	Device		"Configured Video Device"
	DefaultDepth	24
EndSection

Section "Module"
	Load	"glx"
EndSection

### Post by Favux on 2008-11-30
Hi abadr,

gali98's been gone a few days.  Hopefully he'll be back soon to bail you out.  I just scanned your build results quickly, hopefully we won't have to go there.  I don't know if Wubi affects things either.  The no Xserver 64 thing looked kind of worrisome as did the not include xorg.conf thing.

What jumps out is your empty xorg.conf.  For comparison this is mine:
```
# xorg.conf (X.Org X Window System server configuration file)
#
# This file was generated by dexconf, the Debian X Configuration tool, using
# values from the debconf database.
#
# Edit this file with caution, and see the xorg.conf manual page.
# (Type "man xorg.conf" at the shell prompt.)
#
# This file is automatically updated on xserver-xorg package upgrades *only*
# if it has not been modified since the last upgrade of the xserver-xorggksudo gedit /etc/X11/xorg.conf &
# package.
#
# If you have edited this file but would like it to be automatically updated
# again, run the following command:
#   sudo dpkg-reconfigure -phigh xserver-xorg

# commented out by update-manager, HAL is now used
# uncommented out 11-27-08 as test for key bindings
Section "InputDevice"
	Identifier	"Generic Keyboard"
	Driver		"kbd"
	Option		"XkbRules"	"xorg"
	Option		"XkbModel"	"pc105"
	Option		"XkbLayout"	"us"
EndSection

# commented out by update-manager, HAL is now used
#Section "InputDevice"
#	Identifier	"Configured Mouse"
#	Driver		"mouse"
#	Option		"CorePointer"
#EndSection

# commented out by update-manager, HAL is now used
#Section "InputDevice"
#	Identifier	"Synaptics Pad"
#	Driver		"synaptics"
#	Option		"SendCoreEvents"	"true"
#	Option		"Device"	"/dev/psaux"
#	Option		"Protocol"	"auto-dev"
#	Option		"HorizEdgeScroll"	"0"
#EndSection

# commented out by update-manager, HAL is now used
Section "InputDevice"
Identifier "stylus"
Driver "wacom"
Option "Type" "stylus"
Option "USB" "on"
Option "Device" "/dev/input/by-path/pci-0000:00:0b.1-usb-0:2.3:1.0-event-mouse"
Option "Button2" "3" # make side-switch a right button
Option "TopX" "225"
Option "TopY" "225"
Option "BottomX" "26300"
Option "BottomY" "16375"
EndSection

# commented out by update-manager, HAL is now used
Section "InputDevice"
Identifier "touch"
Driver "wacom"
Option "Type" "touch"
Option "USB" "on"
Option "Device" "/dev/input/by-path/pci-0000:00:0b.1-usb-0:2.3:1.1-event-"
Option "TopX" "200"
Option "TopY" "225"
Option "BottomX" "4000"
Option "BottomY" "3875"
EndSection

# commented out by update-manager, HAL is now used
Section "InputDevice"
Identifier "eraser"
Driver "wacom"
Option "Type" "eraser"
Option "Device" "/dev/input/by-path/pci-0000:00:0b.1-usb-0:2.3:1.0-event-mouse"
Option "USB" "on"
EndSection

Section "Device"
	Identifier	"Configured Video Device"
	Driver		"nvidia"
	Option		"NoLogo"	"True"
        Option          "RandRRotation"  "on"
EndSection

Section "Monitor"
	Identifier	"Configured Monitor"
EndSection

Section "Screen"
	Identifier	"Default Screen"
	Monitor		"Configured Monitor"
	Device		"Configured Video Device"
	Defaultdepth	24
EndSection

Section "ServerLayout"
	Identifier	"Default Layout"
  screen "Default Screen"
# commented out by update-manager, HAL is now used
#	Inputdevice	"Synaptics Pad"
# commented out by update-manager, HAL is now used
Inputdevice "stylus"	"SendCoreEvents"
# commented out by update-manager, HAL is now used
Inputdevice "touch"	"SendCoreEvents"
# commented out by update-manager, HAL is now used
Inputdevice "eraser"	"SendCoreEvents"
EndSection

Section "Module"
	Load		"glx"
EndSection
```
Notice in the  three <Section "InputDevice"> sections there are entries for stylus, touch, and eraser.  You need these.  Also notice in the <Section "ServerLayout"> part there are three matching "SendCoreEvents".

I'm jealous about the ATI graphics you have, much better than my nVidia graphics.  To get screen rotation you'll need:
```
        Option          "RandRRotation"  "on"
```
in your "Configure Video" section.  Edit:  Apparently only nVidia graphics needs this.  If you're on ATI you need Xorg's "radeon", "fglrx" doesn't support rotation yet.

I am positive that in some threads with "TX2500" in the name I have seen gali98 give or post a TX2500 xorg.conf to folks.  Your best bet would be to find one of those and cut and paste that into your xorg.conf (in /etc/X11).  After backing up your xorg.conf of course.  This would be a much better bet than trying to build your xorg.conf piece by piece using mine as a model.

In my xorg.conf you can see that Intrepid wanted to "#" out everything due to the introduction of HAL.  Don't worry about that, you still have to use xorg.conf to get tablet function.  The reason that I removed the comments from in front of my keyboard section is that HAL also breaks single key key bindings.  So you can't use your "Q" key for screen rotation without reverting to xorg.conf for keyboard.  HAL does handle the touchpad though.

Hopefully all you need is a correct and functioning TX2500 xorg.conf to get up and running.

Good luck.

---

### Post by Favux on 2008-12-03
Hi xjcannonx,

I don't see why not.  You could at least try it.

That's why I wrote the How To.  Although mirosol's original TX2000 How To did cover rotation there seemed to be other stuff.  I couldn't find it explained in one How To, just bits and pieces scattered.  The TX1000 has "stylus", "eraser", and "touch" doesn't it?  If you've enabled wacom on your tablet then the entries are in your xorg.conf, correct?  The TX1000 digitizer is a wacom right?  Just not an active digitizer.  The only other thing you need is:
```
Option   "Rotation"   "on"
```
in your video section in xorg.conf, if it isn't already there.

The how to is at:

   [http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=996830]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=996830")

You might have to edit the script to reflect your stylus etc.  Let me know how it works.

Good luck!

### Post by martinjochimsen on 2008-12-09
to phraustbyte

I just took a look at your xorg and I see that there is missing some impotent stuff about the wacomdriver. Did you follow galis guide from post 5?
After I had followed his guide my xorg looked just like yours, but I had an old xorg which I copy/pasted from. Try to copy the parts from my xorg about the stylus, touch and eraser. Be aware that you might do this part from galis guide just to be sure:

```
Now Maximize the termial....
now in the termial type :

Code:

reset

dmesg | grep Wacom

there should be two lines similar to this:

Code:

[ 45.460644] input: Wacom ISDv4 93 as /devices/pci0000:00/0000:00:0b.1/usb2/2-2/2-2.3/2-2.3:1.0/input/input9
[ 45.478030] input: Wacom ISDv4 93 as /devices/pci0000:00/0000:00:0b.1/usb2/2-2/2-2.3/2-2.3:1.1/input/input10


now do:

Code:

ls -l /dev/input/by-path

That should give you something similar to:


Code:

lrwxrwxrwx 1 root root 9 2008-07-27 12:07 pci-0000:00:0b.1-usb-0:2.3:1.0-event-mouse -> ../event9
lrwxrwxrwx 1 root root 9 2008-07-27 12:07 pci-0000:00:0b.1-usb-0:2.3:1.0-mouse -> ../mouse1
lrwxrwxrwx 1 root root 9 2008-07-27 12:07 pci-0000:00:0b.1-usb-0:2.3:1.1- -> ../mouse2
lrwxrwxrwx 1 root root 10 2008-07-27 12:07 pci-0000:00:0b.1-usb-0:2.3:1.1-event- -> ../event10
lrwxrwxrwx 1 root root 9 2008-07-27 12:07 platform-i8042-serio-0-event-kbd -> ../event1
lrwxrwxrwx 1 root root 10 2008-07-27 12:07 platform-i8042-serio-1-event-mouse -> ../event11
lrwxrwxrwx 1 root root 9 2008-07-27 12:07 platform-i8042-serio-1-mouse -> ../mouse3
lrwxrwxrwx 1 root root 9 2008-07-27 12:07 platform-pcspkr-event-spkr -> ../event2


Now find the file that matches the output of dmesg i.e:

input9 (from dmesg) matches with event9 (in the ls command) So The File

pci-0000:00:0b.1-usb-0:2.3:1.0-event-mouse

is one that we need.

next input10 (from dmesg) matches with event10 (in the ls command) So The File

pci-0000:00:0b.1-usb-0:2.3:1.1-event-

is the other we need.

Now just amend your xorg.conf with those two names that you just got. The one ending with "mouse" should be in the stylus and eraser sections
and the one ending in "event-" should be in the touch section.
In theory since we have the same basic laptops these files should be the same as mine but you need to check....
If you have anything other than a tx2000 it probably will be different.

And that should be it.

```


Is your graphiccard a ATI Radeon 3200 HD?
I found out that when I deactived the fglrx-driver in Hardware Drivers the touchscreen and especially the rotation worked much better. Actually the rotation doesn't work with fglrx-driver activated.

Martin .-.)

### Post by tekrytor on 2008-12-10
[SOLVED] Wacom touchscreen installed on HP tx2510us running Intrepid 8.10 by using gali98's procedure.
[http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=870640]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=870640")

Notes:

Comments:
It took me a few attempts over a few days/weeks, and a 4 am late nighter with it tonight; but now it works GREAT now and was really worth the effort! The only things not yet working on this fantastic lil notebook are the IR remote, bluetooth, printer, and the fingerprint ID and I'm not sure I want to even use Cheney's lil brother anyway. ### Post by tekrytor on 2008-12-10
> **phraustbyte said:**
> I have done this. Few things are missing from my xorg.conf. I have no section called "Synaptics Touchpad" or otherwise. I added the lines from your post cross-referanced with the post #5. This actually crashed my xserver (Came up with a black screen). I reset the xorg.conf file from the terminal (ctrl-alt-f1) and reset the computer. Its all back to working, but the tablet doesn't work (Which makes sense, actually). Just another note, if I run wacomcpl, it doesn't show any device at all. I also tried reseting using your ctrl-alt-bksp advice. This resets the x-server, but doesn't help the problem.


I just went through this on my tx2510 successfully, touchscreen and calibration are now working. 

I think Martin is pointing you in the right direction. I had trouble getting the right "pci-0000:00:0b.1-usb-0:2.3:1.1-event-" lines in my xorg.conf file. I got lucky with "stylus" and "erasure" but "touch" was missing in the calibration screen. When I checked my edit in xorg.conf, I was missing only the silly little "-" following "event-". Adding that hyphen/dash made the touchscreen work with my finger, the pen already worked. It also made the "Touch Button" show up in the calibration. Therefore, I suspect that you're xorg.conf is missing something, as Martin suggested. The tough part for me was deciding which lines to use. 

You want only the parts of the lines that looks something like this:
pci-0000:00:0b.1-usb-0:2.3:1.1-event-

Follow Gali98's instructions about this part very closely. It's a bit confusing to sort out the lines, but it's apparently what makes it all work. If nothing else, you could probably try then one at a time to see which works. You just need to have a way to recover your backup xorg.conf if it goes crazy on you. I booted to an alternate rev offered by GRUB to get into mine on another occasion where I hosed my xorg.conf, and then used cp to replace the xorg file with the backup. Then I was back where I started.

The values vary by system hardware apparently, I think the pci-xxxx: portion is the PCI port info and the USB follows, etc. This is probably how the touchscreen interfaces with the motherboard and OS, and is essential to making it all work. I think you are VERY close to having iot working.  

I posted my xorg.conf file for comparison. Use it or its parts at your own risk. This one has the touchscreen working well but without rotation. 

Good luck and keep us posted.

tekrytor

---

### Post by martinjochimsen on 2008-12-10
How I got the wacom-driver to work when I start my laptop:

sudo nano /etc/modules
add wacom
ctrl-o (save)
ctrl-x (exit)
reboot the computer

It worked for me!!!

Martin :-)

### Post by tekrytor on 2008-12-13

I WAS using the non-ubuntu-supported ati driver, since my tx2510 has ati chipset, and the graphics were great. If yours also has the ati graphics set, you might try it too. You have to set your repositories to allow the non-ubuntu stuff though.

If you have any other graphic chipset, do NOT use the ATI driver, it will not work and could possibly damage your system, and will possibly render your Ubuntu installation unusable, etc.

### Post by Riverhed on 2008-12-16
Since my last post I figured out my sound issues and I've found an acceptable-enough-for-me temporary fix for the stylus. I remapped the side-button from right-click to left-click and set my mouse preferences so that if I hold left-click it does a right-click. So now I have perfect tracking of my stylus and I can use that button to click and right-click. It would be nice to have the pressure sensitivity so I could use it the way it's supposed to be, but at least I can use the stylus in the meantime.

Thanks to everyone for the advice and how-to's.

### Post by Loïc2 on 2008-12-18
I've just backported i386 and amd64 0.8.6 packages (from Jaunty) for Intrepid, they are on the [[COLOR="DarkRed"]Community wiki documentation[/COLOR]]("https://help.ubuntu.com/community/Wacom") along with install instructions.

They should save compiling and installing the new drivers by hand, you can edit your howtos (saves a lot of time/confusion/problems).

I've tested them on amd64 and they work OK. Remember you still have to edit your xorg.conf properly ;)
Please test them and report if they work for you at [https://bugs.launchpad.net/intrepid-...ts/+bug/309531](https://bugs.launchpad.net/intrepid-...ts/+bug/309531) so they can be included in the -backport repositories.

If you've messed up your configuration when trying to compile and install the drivers, you can undo most changes with the instructions at [https://help.ubuntu.com/community/Wacom/LatestDriver](https://help.ubuntu.com/community/Wacom/LatestDriver) (just do the sudo ./uninstall step), then reinstalling the 0.8.4 drivers from the repositories or the 0.8.6 from the documentation.

---

### Post by Favux on 2008-12-19
Hi Mars Thrax,

Which version of Ubuntu are you on?  Which kernel do you have?
```
uname -r
```
in a terminal.

It sounds like a problem with your video card driver.  What video chipset are you running?  It could also be a Compiz bug.  I'm running Compiz without a problem, so it would have to be a video card specific bug.  And then of course one or both of them could be having a problem with Xserver.  If you can update your video driver, try that.  If there are alternate video drivers for your video card which are they?

Because you are not seeing anything in wacomcpl it does not sound like the wacom kernel module is sensing any input.  It may be you are just getting stylus input through HAL, which does not use xorg.conf.  Your xorg.conf may be improperly configured.

Does your tablet have other inputs besides the stylus?  Like eraser, side button, or touch.  If so which ones?

For a start why don't you post the output of:
```
dmesg | grep Wacom
```
in a terminal.  Also please post your xorg.conf located in:
```
/etc/X11/xorg.conf
```

Also have you looked at the laptoptestingteam site?  There is one Toshiba Portege 700 listed:

   [https://wiki.ubuntu.com/LaptopTestingTeam/ToshibaPortegeM700]("https://wiki.ubuntu.com/LaptopTestingTeam/ToshibaPortegeM700")

This may be helpful.

### Post by Favux on 2008-12-19
Hi Mars Thrax,

I should have asked you to explain in more detail what you mean by:
> Second, my touchscreen is responding, but is not calibrated properly.
Do you mean not responding properly to touch, or to the sylus,  or eraser and the side button, or to everything?  Also what are the "cursor" references for?  My impression is that "cursor" is for a seperate plug-in Wacom graphics tablet where you can use some feature on the Wacom tablet as a mouse?  Does it do anything on your tablet pc?

Ok, regarding the video.  Intel is suppose to have pretty good linux support so this may be a known bug.  Try searching launchpad and bugzilla with the appropriate key words and see if there is a work around.

For me the output of ~$ dmesg | grep Wacom is:
```

[   30.913216] input: Wacom ISDv4 93 as /devices/pci0000:00/0000:00:0b.1/usb2/2-2/2-2.3/2-2.3:1.0/input/input11
[   30.957435] input: Wacom ISDv4 93 as /devices/pci0000:00/0000:00:0b.1/usb2/2-2/2-2.3/2-2.3:1.1/input/input12
[   31.017488] wacom: v1.49:USB Wacom Graphire and Wacom Intuos tablet driver
```
See it not only tells us that the wacom module is installed it tells you what Wacom tablet is used.  It also gives input paths that you can use in xorg.conf.  So you have a serial tablet.  I guess there is no output with this command with a serial tablet.  As a forlorn hope try it again after a fresh reboot, before you've done anything else.

If you know a way to get this type of output for a serial device let me know.

So let's try another way.  In a terminal type:
```
lsmod
```
And look for "wacom", not "linuxwacom".  Also see if there is some sort of serial stuff with "wacom" associated with it.  If you see "wacom" then the module is loaded.  Then try:
```
modinfo -d wacom
```
This should tell us what kind of Wacom tablet you have (and if we're lucky maybe some serial stuff).

This should be enough info. to use "wacdump" and see what it tells us.  Instructions for using "wacdump" are at:

   [http://linuxwacom.sourceforge.net/index.php/howto/wacdump]("http://linuxwacom.sourceforge.net/index.php/howto/wacdump")

Post any of the above results you think are relevant.

Luck!

---

### Post by Mars Thrax on 2008-12-19
Well, I ended up fixing my problem. It turns out that the M700 has a known issue with the current wacom utilities in the respositories. I uninstalled both xserver-xorg-input-wacom and wacom-tools, downloaded the latest sources (0.8.2), and then compiled and installed. It turns out it must have been the touch screen problems that were also causing issues when I rotated the screen, because installing the new driver fixed the visual problems.

So, to recap, in Intrepid, the Toshiba M700 needs at least the 0.8.2 sources (or 0.8.1-6 with the patch, as described [here]("https://bugs.launchpad.net/ubuntu/+source/wacom-tools/+bug/300980")). Then, you can follow [this]("https://help.ubuntu.com/community/Wacom/LatestDriver") guide to install the driver manually. After doing that, you should be able to follow the regular guides for rotating screen and whatnot. Works with Compiz.

Thanks for all the help guys.

---

### Post by Favux on 2008-12-20
Hey Mars Thrax,

Great!  Nice job.  By the way, did you notice in the bug report at Launchpad Martin Sucha, when he's showing his xorg.conf input devices, points out you do not need "cursor" in your xorg.conf !

Yup, like I said it was only there because the Laptop Testing Team had it in their config, but I ended up removing it.

### Post by Loïc2 on 2008-12-20
> **Favux said:**
> Thanks Loïc2,
Could you backport Linux Wacom Project's latest linuxwacom driver 1.0.8.2?

When they'll appear in Jaunty it will be easy, but at the moment Jaunty still has 1.0.8.1.6 (and I'm not sure Debian has them either, since our wacom drivers are pulled from Debian).

> **Favux said:**
> 
Do you know how, in Intrepid, to generate a correctly configured xorg.conf?  Right now it seems the only way to get a properly configured xorg.conf is to "forward"port a Hardy or earlier config.conf.  It is not clear to me what is missing in Intrepid that prevents the configured config.conf from being generated.  This is causing a lot of problems for folks with newer tablet pc's who are installing Ubuntu for the first time.

You still need to add the lines by hand (there's example lines in the guides). The configuration was never autogenerated, Feisty (and some other distributions than Ubuntu) generate xorg.conf with default wacom lines, but they don't correspond to people's hardware (unless you happen to have stylus, cursor and eraser ;) all 3 but nothing else, that's not common).

A new GUI is being developed, you can find more information on the ubuntu-x mailing list and there's a wiki page at [https://wiki.ubuntu.com/X/Blueprints/WacomTabletsUi](https://wiki.ubuntu.com/X/Blueprints/WacomTabletsUi)

It's still unsure what will get into it, but the programmer seem to think it will be ready for Jaunty.

> **Favux said:**
> 
Also have you heard if the developers have figured a way around HAL's limitations so that we no longer need xorg.conf?  Some sort of new magical fdi file I suppose.  They just had the big Jaunty conference but I couldn't find anything on it.  I did see they have made touchscreen support a high priority.

The HAL problems aren't going to go away soon. HAL only supports one device, and HAL people consider it's not HAL job to be Xorg configuration store (with valid arguments). The DBUS method is being investigated by only one person (discussion in linuxwacom-discuss/devel mailing lists), but at the moment it crashes X, and it's not sure when that could be sorted out. Xorg people still haven't decided what they're going to use for wacom devices hotplugging, so there's actually no solution we can be sure would be accepted by them.

In the meantime, the wacom GUI would solve some problems, especially with TabletPC who don't need hotplugging anyway (for on the fly preferences setting, you can already do that, hotplugging is only necessary for Wacom USB tablet users, like the Intuos, Cintiq, Bamboo, Graphire.)

Some touch-screen aren't using wacom drivers. They could possibly eventually work with evdev, I don't know for sure.

---

### Post by Loïc2 on 2008-12-21
Well, if you've read the ubuntu-x mailing list and the wiki page for the GUI that is being developed, I don't think there's anything more to do (unless you have any suggestion). I'm not sure petitionning for Ubuntu to support wacom device now they started working on it is going to be that useful ;)

For hotplug, it's not really in Ubuntu's hand. It's between Xorg and Linuxwacom...

Of course, all Linux wacom users should register on the Wacom manufacturer site (and if you're using a TabletPC you should also get in touch with its manufacturer), but I guess you've already done that.

---

### Post by Loïc2 on 2008-12-25
> **Favux said:**
> Is there a petition we can sign?  Is there a site we can go and register our support?  Is there anyway to indicate we would like Ubuntu to work on Wacom issues?

Actually there's something you (and other TabletPC users) can help with - and without your help there's not much chance the situation will improve.

I've posted not long ago asking people to test backported wacom packages from Jaunty to Intrepid - the packages are at [https://bugs.launchpad.net/intrepid-backports/+bug/309531](https://bugs.launchpad.net/intrepid-backports/+bug/309531) and feedback need to be given there.

At the moment, only **two** persons have tested them and reported their results. That's far from stellar, and without more input and interest from Ubuntu users there's not much chance the TabletPC situation is ever going to improve. Considering the number of TabletPC models out there, we need far more input than for Wacom graphic tablets.

So trying the backported packages is a first step. Then, if you (not "you" personally, maybe you're one of the two people that already tested the packages, but "you" as "everyone reading this thread") really want to make the problem solved in future versions (Jaunty and latter) installing Jaunty alpha or beta releases on a spare partition regularly and testing the packages, then reporting the bugs in Launchpad (and keeping an eye on these bugs to offer answers and testing if needed) would make a huge difference.

---

### Post by tekrytor on 2008-12-26
Subtopic 1: Webcam on HP tx2510us Tablet PC running Ubuntu 8.10
===============================================================

> First recommendation would be to try to install the program "cheese" and see if your webcam works with that.

From your recommendation, I installed 'cheese', and (perhaps foolhardily) additionally 'cameramonitor' and 'vgrabbj', all three at the same time from the Synaptic Package Manager (no compile, etc necessary, very simple). I found these by searching in Synaptic for webcam, and discounting any specialized driver associated packages. 

It works great. I now have functional webcam with audio (using the 'toshiba' audio fix), in Ekiga, and several other video apps.

Subtopic 2: HP tx2500 Configuration Summary
===========================================

I'm quite happy with my Ubuntu 8.10 config. Only a few issues left for 100% functionality equivalent to Windows, but with Ubuntu SPEED and more configuration options. This is a much faster machine thanks to Ubuntu.

The fixes I've done so far to get to this level are all in this thread:

0. Install Ubuntu 8.10 (64-bit).
1. Install Broadcom wifi driver.
2. Used 'wacom' touchscreen install tutorial from gali98.
3. Fixed sound by appending (less quotes):
   "options snd-hda-intel index=0 model=toshiba position_fix=1" 
     to the file /etc/modprobe.d - from gali98. 
4. Used 'rotation' config from Favum, incuding returning to non-ATI driver.
5. Used 'webcam' recommendation from th89 (plus 2 others mentioned above).

NOTE: I'll edit this page ASAP to post links to 1-4 above postings; but for now, you can search this thread for the above postings.


Current issues
==============
 (on 'my' HP tx2510us)

Rotation
--------
Currently running kernel 2.6.27-11-generic, after updating from 2.6.27-10-generic kernel (not sure exactly which, will update ASAP), the rotation fix was corrupted. It now works fine in standard position, but rotation crashes. Not sure what to do about this yet. This is the biggest problem currently.

Fingerscan
----------
Not used, nor interested; but it might be good to know how to config this.

Audio
-----
Volume settings are linear, not logarithmic as normal in audio systems. This means that I/you have to turn up the volume most of the way to get any discernible output. Decreasing the volume to less than around 75% results in no discernible audio output. The audio range is therefore very limited and can be difficult to optimize in some applications. A fix would be nice.

---

### Post by Favux on 2009-01-15
Hi natacho,

Plenty of TX2500 users have a working tablet using gali98's tutorial and the xorg.conf you got at the HOW TO.  So what are we doing different?

Let's review what we know.  You have a HP Pavillion TX2500.  You've installed Ubuntu 8.10 64 bits.  Your kernel is 2.6.27-9 generic.  You have the working TX2500 xorg.conf from my HOW TO installed in "/etc/X11/".

So questions.  Are you sure it is a TX2500?  What is the exact model #?  On the bottom/back is a plate with the model #.  The 64-bit install was AMD-64?

Does the tablet work in vista?  Do you have stylus, side switch, eraser and touch?

Since you have followed galip98's tutorial twice there should be a linuxwacom kernel module.  It will be called "wacom".  Try the following.  The two commands previously and:
```
dmesg
```
```
modinfo -d wacom
```

Sorry this is taking so long.  But this is a mystery.  I will go through your output from your first gali98 run through more carefully.

---

### Post by Favux on 2009-01-15
Also natacho,

When you look in:

"/usr/lib/xorg/modules/input"  you should see a file called "wacom_drv.so"

and in:

"/lib/modules/'uname -r'/kernel/drivers/input/tablet"  you should see a file called "wacom.ko"  (where 'uname -r' is the name of your current kernel).

---

wacom                  31368  0 
usbcore               175376  9 wacom,btusb,uvcvideo,usb_storage,usbhid,libusual,ehci_hcd,ohci_hcd
ignacio@ignacio-laptop:~$ 

```
Thanks for the help

---

### Post by Favux on 2009-01-16
Hi natacho,

OK, now we're getting somewhere.  So you had activity you didn't notice and lost on reboot.  Martinjochimsen ran into the same problem and posted a fix, I think on this thread.  He just posted it on another thread, let me get it.

From martinjochimsen:
> I had the same problem until I added "wacom" to /etc/modules, then it worked everytime.
```
sudo nano /etc/modules
add wacom (fx at the bottom)
crtl-o (save)
crtl-x (exit)
```
> My /etc/modules looks like this:
```
# /etc/modules: kernel modules to load at boot time.
#
# This file contains the names of kernel modules that should be loaded
# at boot time, one per line. Lines beginning with "#" are ignored.

fuse
lp
wacom
powernow-k8
```
Let's see if this works natacho.

---

### Post by Favux on 2009-03-06
Hi cenzorrll,

The reason I thought you had a TX2z is that Rene's patch is to give the N-trig digitizer functionality with the linuxwacom drivers.

Since you do have a TX2500 you probably need to correctly configure your xorg.conf.  There is a TX2500 xorg.conf for you to download here:

[http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?p=6546012#post6546012]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?p=6546012#post6546012")

Be sure and backup yours before you do anything.  Then compare the downloaded one to yours.  Likely you can just copy yours over.

When wacomcpl doesn't see stylus, eraser, and touch it could mean something is wrong with your linuxwacom driver install.  Maybe Rene's patch has messed it up?  Or you need to copy the module again to the right directory or use martinjochimsen's fix.  All described on the linked thread.  Or it could just mean your xorg.conf is incorrectly configured and the wacom features aren't available to X.

Good luck!

---

### Post by cenzorrll on 2009-03-07
FINALLY! thank you very much for sending that link, i kind of feel dumb that i didn't find it in my searching, but it definitely solved all my problems. it must have been that i was using 8.1-6 and not 8.2-2 (i can't think of anything else i did differently) the tutorial was excellent.

by the way, i don't know if this is true with anyone else, but i definitely didn't have a "serverLayout" section or a synaptics touchpad in the device inputs

---

### Post by Favux on 2009-03-07
Hi cenzorrll,

Great!  Glad everything is working now.  Good job.  Whether 0.8.1-6 was the culprit.  Who knows?

Right with Intrepid and HAL(hardware abstraction layer) they were deprecating xorg.conf and a lot of stuff doesn't show up in it.  That's caused a lot of people problems, so you're not alone.  HAL should be able to run your Synaptic TouchPad fine (through it's .fdi file) so it can be commented out in your xorg.conf (and "ServerLayout").  I strongly recommend keeping copies of your xorg.conf for different configurations of it and different versions of Ubuntu somewhere safe.

### Post by Favux on 2009-03-23
Hi music10man,

Welcome to Ubuntu!

> I've tried both the version recommended here and the latest version.
I'm not sure what you mean.  Are you talking about the linuxwacom driver version you installed?

You have the same problem as music10man, you have a fresh Intrepid (8.10) xorg.conf that is almost empty.  To get a xorg.conf for a TX2500 go to the link I gave him on post #   .  It's at the bottom of the first post on that thread.  Follow the cautions I gave him.  Back up your xorg.conf, compare, etc.

To edit xorg.conf, in a terminal type (actually copy and paste):
```
gksudo gedit /etc/X11/xorg.conf
```

You probably do not need to compile the kernel.  You could try the linuxwacom driver deb.s at Loic2's Wacom wiki:

[https://help.ubuntu.com/community/Wacom]("https://help.ubuntu.com/community/Wacom")
