### Post by Favux on 2009-03-23
Hi music10man,

Which HP TX do you have?  It is the TX2500 correct?  At least that's what Ebornpl had.

There seem to be two issues.  One you may not have the linuxwacom drivers correctly installed.  Two your xorg.conf is still not configured correctly (as you've noticed).

It's actually not as hard as it seems, so be patient.  I'm guessing that by "following the instructions from the first page" you mean gali98's tutorial on post #3.  Actually I've updated his tutorial and it is here:

[http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=1038949]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=1038949")
(notice the xorg.conf's at the bottom)

But since you're a "newbie" I was trying to make it easier on you by directing you to Loic2's Wacom wiki.  There are AMD_64 linuxwacom deb.s (2 packages) there.  The term deb stands for prepackaged Debian packages.  That means you can download them onto your desktop, double click them and they will install themselves through the Debian Package Manager.  Then Synaptic Package Manager will see them, just as if Synaptic installed them.

Your xorg.conf isn't nearly as bare but it looks like you downloaded the TX2000 xorg.conf not the TX2500.  Your /by-path/pci etc. are the TX2000's not the TX2500's, and yes it makes a difference.  What maybe breaking X is in your "ServerLayout" section you have:
```
	Inputdevice	"Synaptics Pad"
```
without the appropriate "InputDevice" section preceeding it.  Since HAL (hardware abstraction layer) now handles it in Intrepid go ahead and comment it out:
```
#	Inputdevice	"Synaptics Pad"
```
Also there seems to be some new video stuff.  My advice is not to be setting up Compiz or other visual effects or another monitor until you've set up Wacom.  And by the way the proprietary ATI "fglrx" drivers just started supporting rotation and they still don't work right rotating with Compiz enabled.

Hope this is helpful.

Edit:  Oops.  Nevermind.  LOL!

---

### Post by Favux on 2009-03-24
Hi music10man,

Basically I leave them in the xorg.conf because when we got to Intrepid suddenly they weren't there.  The wacom examples had been in the xorg.conf's for several prior versions.  So I leave them in, you don't have to.  And I have safe backups.

You don't need the keyboard, mouse, and synaptic touchpad.  You could remove them.  Except if you want to bind a single key (like your Q key) for screen rotation.  Then you need keyboard.  On the linuxwacom HOW TO I link to here:

[http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?p=6274392#post6274392]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?p=6274392#post6274392")

Which explains rotation, Compiz and "fglrx", and key binding.

### Post by Favux on 2009-03-24
Hi Ebornpl,

Thank you for the follow-up.  I'm glad Wacom is working!
> ended up with X not starting - that's the reason for the command prompt instead of GUI while booting, right?).
Correct.  There must have been a format error large enough to break Xserver.

Editing xorg.conf can be surprisingly tricky.  Especially if you change input sections without realizing that means there must be changes in "ServerLayout".
> you can proceed even if you have no visible marks of touch being detected
Sure, the by-path/pci of touch is different from stylus and eraser.  You have to pay pretty close attention to notice that though.

Gali98's pretty busy and doesn't have much time at the moment.  So I doubt he'll update his tutorial.  That's why I've updated his tutorial (on the link above).  But he is still around.  He just helped me out the other day with Wacom symlinks rules.

### Post by Favux on 2009-03-26
Hi music10man,

That's my understanding.  But there is rapid progress with the drivers and and Compiz.  ATI released a bunch of code a couple months ago.  Although, admittedly it mostly seems to have been the 2-D stuff.  Rotation wasn't even supported until Sept. '08 (Catalyst 8.9).  Now ATI has announced they're dropping support for some older chipsets in linux (actually they say moving support over to the OSS team with some of their support) while they continue with "fglrx" developement for the new chipsets.  So who knows?

So you could go back to the proprietary "fglrx" driver if you want, just not with Compiz.  There is a command you might have to run to enable rotation though.  See details on the Rotation HOW TO.

### Post by Favux on 2009-03-31
Hi tdeboeser,

The TX2000 has nvidia graphics.  The TX2500 changes to ATI graphics.  The TX2z changes from the Wacom digitizer to the N-trig digitizer.  It should be on the plate on the bottom of your laptop.  Admittedly HP sometimes confuses the issue by using TX2000 as a generic TX2* series kind of label.

xorg.conf.txt I'm guessing is from Rene and is definitely not correct.  It's for a TX2z I think.  xorg.conf.almost.txt actually looks pretty good for a TX2000.

Since you are sure it is a TX2000 use the xorg.conf at the bottom of the first post here:

[http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=1038949]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=1038949")

Back up your xorg.conf and compare the two.

Edit:  I should mention the xorg.conf's are configured for Intrepid.

### Post by Favux on 2009-04-01
Hi tom de,

Our models are nearly identical, I have the TX2110us.  The xorg.conf you got at the bottom of the tutorial should work fine, and I seriously doubt that is the problem.

To rule out a hardware problem if you still have a Windows partition boot in there.  Most likely it's a linuxwacom problem.  And the reason you are seeing nothing in wacomcpl is due to it.

So if you:
```
dmesg | grep [Ww]acom
```
do you see the wacom kernel module?  Did you try:
```
lsmod

modinfo -d wacom
```
Have you modprobed it?

This could be a mismatch between the version of linuxwacom drivers you installed and the version of wacom-tools you installed.  They need to be the same version.  Not a good thing if they are different as you can see and according to the LWP it can break X.

All that said the digitizer and touchscreen are in effect two separate units on our model (as n-trig is fond of pointing out) so theoretically...

Edit:  You are running on Intrepid, correct?  If not there is a problem with using the Synaptic TouchPad in Hardy or earlier.  As detailed on the tutorial linked above it will confuse linuxwacom and needs to be renamed Synaptic Pad and also the corresponding entry in "ServerLayout".

---

### Post by tdeboeser on 2009-04-02
**[SIZE="5"]Got it, Got it, Got it!!! w00t!!![/SIZE]**

Ok, my wacomcpl doesn't work **but** my stylus works!

Ok, going on the mismatch possibility, suggested by Favux:

> 
This could be a mismatch between the version of linuxwacom drivers you installed and the version of wacom-tools you installed. They need to be the same version. Not a good thing if they are different as you can see and according to the LWP it can break X.


I found it wasn't just a mismatch with the wacom-tools package from the ubuntu Ibex repo's, but also with the the xserver-xorg-input-wacom package. I uninstalled both, THEN recompilied the linuxwacom-0.8.2-2.  



I had to then copy the the Xorg wacom_drv.so to the xorg modules dir:

```

sudo cp linuxwacom-0.8.2-2/prebuilt/64/wacom_drv.so /usr/lib/xorg/modules/input/.

```

This means the Ibex repo's for wacom are older than the modules/tools in the linuxwacom tar.  

In my case I'm happy, so far.  Now its on to the apps...

Thanks Favux!!

---

### Post by joutsen on 2009-04-05
Thanks for an excellent thread. Using the guidelines here, I have set up a working finger-friendly desktop environment with AWN and such.

However, one problem remains: I lose "touch" when I suspend/resume the laptop.

Cause: It looks like the USB devices are virtually unplugged/plugged during suspend/resume. This can and will cause the device ids to change, sometimes, perhaps always after second suspend/resume after boot. Unfortunately, the devices in /dev/input are not updated to match the change, and touch is lost (curiously, the pen works, always).

Here's a snippet from dmesg, after this reassignment has happened:
> [   40.023215] input: Wacom ISDv4 93 as /devices/pci0000:00/0000:00:0b.1/usb2/2-2/2-2.3/2-2.3:1.0/input/input10
[   40.083879] input: Wacom ISDv4 93 as /devices/pci0000:00/0000:00:0b.1/usb2/2-2/2-2.3/2-2.3:1.1/input/input11
[   40.137253] wacom: v1.49:USB Wacom Graphire and Wacom Intuos tablet driver
[ 1632.180306] input: Wacom ISDv4 93 as /devices/pci0000:00/0000:00:0b.0/usb1/1-2/1-2.3/1-2.3:1.0/input/input13
[ 1632.256383] input: Wacom ISDv4 93 as /devices/pci0000:00/0000:00:0b.0/usb1/1-2/1-2.3/1-2.3:1.1/input/input14

Things I have tried: Changed to use the /dev/input/usb-Tablet_ISD-V4-event-mouse for pen and /dev/input/wacom for touch in xorg.conf. These are easier on the eye than the by-path alternatives, and work just fine, but do not get any more updated after suspend/resume. I have also tried to restart udev, but this has not resulted in updated devices in /dev/input.

Any ideas?

---

### Post by joutsen on 2009-04-05
Some more information:

After "touch" has been lost due to suspend/resume:
[LIST]
[*]/etc/init.d/udev stop and /etc/init.d/udev start will restore functionality
[*]/etc/init.d/udev restart will not.
[*]Jaunty promises a new function, /etc/init.d/udev refresh-devices
[/LIST]

Since full restart of udev at every resume seems wrought with peril, I think I will wait for Jaunty. Unless someone knows of a safe way to accomplish the refresh in Intrepid?

### Post by Favux on 2009-04-05
Hi joutsen,

The old hotplug commands are ctrl-alt-F1 and then ctrl-alt-F7.  That's what I use if Wacom doesn't resume after suspend.  Actually, a lot of times just ctrl-alt-F1 works for me.  It pops in and out of the terminal.

The reason the stylus keeps working is that HAL with its 10-wacom.fdi file has taken over control of the stylus.  Correct udev format is "wacom" for stylus and eraser and "wacom-touch" for touch.  See appendix 3 here:  [http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=1038949](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=1038949)

Hotplug has been an issue.  There are some hotplug bugfixes in the latest.  Hopefully they'll work.

Edit:  Don't try Jaunty yet.  I have an announcement I'll post it a little while you'll want to see first.

---

### Post by Favux on 2009-04-05
Hi Everyone,

This is for Jaunty users or people preparing to move to Jaunty.  This announcement comes from Timo Aaltonen by way of Loïc2.  This will fill in some background.
> **Timo Aaltonen** (3-24-09):
For jaunty, there's a new wacom-tools in my PPA which should do proper 
input hotplugging by using a hal callout program to set up the extra 
devices that the fdi file lists the hardware should support. It should 
also work on builtin serial devices like on tablet laptops. The patches, 
including some bugfixes, are borrowed from Fedora.

The quote is from:

[https://lists.ubuntu.com/archives/ubuntu-devel/2009-March/027865.html](https://lists.ubuntu.com/archives/ubuntu-devel/2009-March/027865.html)

I'm guessing the callout program uses the .fdi file to query dBUS?  So they have figured out multiple input devices for HAL.  Or think they have.  This should offer the proper hotplug support through HAL/.fdi that Intrepid and Jaunty were meant to have.

If you are **interested in testing** Timo Aaltonen has pre-packaged the modified linuxwacom xserver-xorg-input-wacom 0.8.2-2 and wacom-tools 0.8.2-2 for you on his ppa (3-24-09).   Note this includes a modified 10-wacom.fdi file:

[https://launchpad.net/~tjaalton/+archive/ppa](https://launchpad.net/~tjaalton/+archive/ppa)

Then click on:

wacom-tools - 1:08.2.2-OubuntuO.2

Update(4-9-09): Above link is now invalid. Timo's ppa has been accepted already. It's in the repositories. Either check Synaptics in Jaunty or go to: [http://packages.ubuntu.com/](http://packages.ubuntu.com/) and select Jaunty. Then X Window System software. It's listed as xserver-xorg-input-wacom.

You will see the i386 and amd64 debs.  You use them to upgrade from the 0.8.1-6 versions that come with Jaunty.  Since Fedora patches support hotplugging through HAL you should not need to configure your xorg.conf.  I'm assuming you can calibrate through wacomcpl.  You will have to re-enable each tool with Gimp, etc.  This should not only work for hot-plugging usb Wacom tablets and usb tablet pc's but also serial tablets and tablet pc's!

**If you are testing** it is important for you to give feed back to this lauchpad site **[FFe] Please allow a new version of wacom-tools** posted (4-4-09):

[https://bugs.launchpad.net/ubuntu/+source/wacom-tools/+bug/355340](https://bugs.launchpad.net/ubuntu/+source/wacom-tools/+bug/355340)

If enough positive feedback is received there is a chance they will update the Jaunty repository to the patched 0.8.2-2.  This could finally get Wacom on Ubuntu close to where we want it.

Good luck!

---

### Post by Favux on 2009-04-12
Hi Everyone,

This is a continuation of post #476.  It looks like there may be a few glitches with the non-xorg.conf HAL/.fdi file dBUS method in Jaunty.  While that shakes out it appears you can still get Wacom in Jaunty.  Just go to the Compile HOW TO:  [http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=1038949](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=1038949) and compile 0.8.3-2.  Make sure that libhal1-dev is not installed when you compile, otherwise you'll get unwanted HAL features.

Hi daddypawid,

I have a TX2110us also.

---

### Post by Favux on 2009-09-18
Hi Toy Machine,

In Jaunty you use the wacom.fdi instead of xorg.conf.  Wacomcpl won't work if in a terminal:
```
xsetwacom list
```
is blank.  To see what HAL is calling your Wacom devices enter in a terminal:
```
xinput --list
```
To get a .fdi that parses the names correctly into linuxwacom names and otherwise set up in Jaunty see "Jaunty Users" near the top here:  [http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?p=6546012#post6546012](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?p=6546012#post6546012)  And follow the link in 1) to gali98's Jaunty HOW TO in post #104.  Then to finish setting up wacomcpl follow "Section 3:  Calibrating your tablet pc" below "Jaunty Users".

Hope this helps.

---

### Post by Toy Machine on 2009-09-18
> **Favux said:**
> Hi Toy Machine,

In Jaunty you use the wacom.fdi instead of xorg.conf.  Wacomcpl won't work if in a terminal:
```
xsetwacom list
```
is blank.  To see what HAL is calling your Wacom devices enter in a terminal:
```
xinput --list
```
To get a .fdi that parses the names correctly into linuxwacom names and otherwise set up in Jaunty see "Jaunty Users" near the top here:  [http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?p=6546012#post6546012](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?p=6546012#post6546012)  And follow the link in 1) to gali98's Jaunty HOW TO in post #104.  Then to finish setting up wacomcpl follow "Section 3:  Calibrating your tablet pc" below "Jaunty Users".

Hope this helps.
